Hawd with Narrow Top and Wide Bottom: The Kathir Water Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on impurity in a basin with varying dimensions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the detailed Hanafi ruling on impurity falling into a hawd with a narrow top and wide bottom, distinguishing between gradual and sudden falls, and evaluate the intra-madhab disagreement.

Core Idea
If impure water falls gradually into abundant water, it becomes pure; falling all at once contaminates.

This passage from al-Khulasa addresses a unique scenario: a basin with a narrow top (less than 10x10) and a wide bottom (10x10). If impurity affects the top water and then it falls into the bottom, later Hanafi scholars differed on whether the whole becomes impure. The text presents a detailed answer based on the manner of fall, illustrating the Hanafi principle of kathir water's ability to overcome minimal impurities when introduced gradually.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and identify the point of contention
Clearly describe the basin: top area less than 10x10, bottom area 10x10. Impurity (e.g., wine drop) falls into the top, then top water mixes with bottom. The dispute is whether the bottom water remains pure.
The top is qalil (<10x10) but connected to kathir bottom when water flows.
2
Outline the detailed answer (tafseel)
Two cases: (1) If impure top water falls into bottom all at once (jumlatan), the whole is impure because impurity dominates in one moment. (2) If it falls gradually (ala al-tadrij), the water is pure because the abundant water overcomes the impurity part by part.
The distinction hinges on the manner of mixing.
3
Identify the opposing view
Some later Hanafi scholars said the water never becomes pure, analogizing to qalil water: once impure, it remains impure even if it later spreads.
This opposition relies on a strict analogy with isolated qalil water.
4
Analyze the rationale
The detailed view uses the principle that kathir water (10x10 and not changing properties) can dilute impurities if introduced gradually. The opposing view treats the top water as independently impure, ignoring the connection to abundant water.
Al-Siraj al-Hindi favored the detailed view, calling it 'ashbah' (more similar to the principles).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الخلاصة : ولو كان أعلاه أقل من عشر في عشر وأسفله عشر في عشر ووقعت قطرة خمر أو توضأ منه رجل ثم انتقص الماء وصار عشراً في عشر اختلف المتأخرون فيه، وينبغي أن يكون الجواب على التفصيل: إن كان الماء الذي تنجس في أعلى الحوض أكثر من الماء الذي في أسفله ووقع الماء النجس في الأسفل جملة كان الماء نجساً. ويصير النجس غالباً على الطاهر في قت واحد، وإن وقع الماء النجس في أسفل الحوض على التدريج كان طاهراً. وقال بعضهم : لا يطهر كالماء القليل إذا وقعت فيه نجاسة ثم انبسط ا هـ . وذكر السراج الهندي أن الأشبه الجواز
And in al-Khulasa: If its top is less than ten by ten and its bottom is ten by ten, and a drop of wine falls or a man performs wudu from it, then the water decreases and becomes ten by ten, the later scholars differed about it. And it should be that the answer is detailed: If the water that became impure in the top of the basin is more than the water in its bottom, and the impure water falls into the bottom all at once, then the water is impure, because the impurity becomes dominant over the pure in one moment. And if the impure water fell into the bottom of the basin gradually, it is pure. And some said: It does not become pure, like little water if an impurity falls into it then spreads. End quote. And al-Siraj al-Hindi mentioned that the more similar (al-ashbah) is permissibility.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute among later Hanafi scholars about a basin that has a narrow top (less than 10x10) but a wide bottom (10x10). If a drop of wine falls into the top, or a man performs wudu from the top (making the water musta'mal), and then the water level decreases so that the surface becomes 10x10 (i.e., the top shrinks? Actually the text says the water decreases and becomes 10x10 – perhaps meaning the top area becomes 10x10? Or the overall water decreases? The scenario is ambiguous but the key point is the contamination in the top part). The solution is detailed: if the water that became impure in the top is more than the water in the bottom, and it falls into the bottom all at once, the whole becomes impure because impurity dominates. If it falls gradually, it is pure because it mixes with the abundant water part by part. Some scholars said it never becomes pure, analogizing to little water that gets impurity and then spreads (i.e., the whole becomes impure). Al-Siraj al-Hindi stated that the more similar view (ashbah) is that it is permissible (i.e., pure). This reflects a difference in applying the principle of kathir to mixed scenarios.

Key Terms
جملة (jumlatan): All at once (as opposed to gradually); falling in one go
على التدريج (ala al-tadrij): Gradually, drop by drop or in succession

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario described, when does the water of the basin become pure according to the detailed answer?
A) When the impure water falls into the bottom all at once
B) When the impure water falls gradually into the bottom
C) When the water level decreases to 10x10
D) When the top part becomes dry

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows purification of water that becomes contaminated in a narrow part if it gradually mixes with abundant water.

Wudu from Channels and Frozen Basins: Connectivity Determines Validity
Rulings on water connectivity for wudu validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that water connectivity determines the validity of wudu in cases of channels, ice holes, and reed thickets.

Core Idea
Water connectivity, not superficial barriers, determines whether wudu is valid in physically separated volumes.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents three practical scenarios where the kathir/qalil distinction is applied: a basin with channels (mashari'), a frozen basin, and a reed thicket. In each case, the key principle is whether the water you use is physically connected to a large body of water. The rulings are derived through qiyas (analogy) to the standard cases of small and large basins.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The passage covers: (a) a hawd with mashari' (channels), (b) a frozen hawd, and (c) a thicket (al-ajjam). Each tests the boundary condition of water connectivity.
Note that some scenarios have sub-cases.
2
Analyze the mashari' cases
Two sub-cases: (i) water in the channel is connected to the planks and not agitated → like a small basin (qalil), wudu invalid. (ii) water is below the planks → like a covered large basin, wudu valid. The illa is the lack of agitation/connection.
Agitation indicates the water is part of the larger body.
3
Apply qiyas to the frozen basin
Two sub-cases: (i) a hole where the water is isolated from the main ice → like a covered basin, wudu valid. (ii) water in the hole is connected to the water beneath → like a bowl (i.e., a small separate basin), wudu invalid.
The bowl analogy highlights that connectivity alone is not enough; the water must be part of a large, open body.
4
Examine the thicket ruling
Reeds (or dense vegetation) do not break water connectivity. Even if reeds grow in the water, the water remains a single great pond (ghadir 'azim), so wudu from the thicket is permissible.
Contrast with planks in mashari'—planks can create isolation if water is not agitated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي التنجيس: حوض عشر في عشر إلا أن له مشارع فتوضأ رجل من مشرعة أو اغتسل والماء متصل بألواح المشرعة لا يضطرب لا يجوز التوضؤ به وإن كان أسفل من الألواح فإنه لا يجوز، وعلله في فتح القدير بأنه في الأول كالحوض الصغير وفي الثاني حوض كبير مسقف، وعلى هذا الحوض الكبير إذا جمد ماؤه فنقب فيه إنسان نقباً فتوضأ من ذلك الموضع فإن كان الماء منفصلاً بأس به لأنه يصير كالحوض المسقف وإن كان متصلاً لا لأنه صار كالقصعة. كذا في التنجيس وغيره. وفي فتح القدير: واتصال القصب بالقصب لا يمنع اتصال الماء ولا يخرجه عن كونه غديراً عظيماً فيجوز لهذا التوضؤ في الأجمة ونحوها ا هـ.
And in al-Tanjis: A basin ten by ten but it has channels (mashari'). A man performed wudu from a channel or bathed, and the water is connected to the planks of the channel, not agitated; it is not permissible to perform wudu with it. And if it is below the planks, then it is not permissible. He explained in Fath al-Qadir that the first is like a small basin, and the second is like a large covered basin. Based on this, if a large basin's water freezes and a man makes a hole in it and performs wudu from that place, if the water is separated (from the main body) it is no harm, because it becomes like a covered basin; if it is connected, it is not, because it becomes like a bowl. Thus in al-Tanjis and others. And in Fath al-Qadir: The connection of reeds to reeds does not prevent the connection of water nor remove it from being a great pond, so it is permissible to perform wudu in thickets (al-ajjam) and the like. End quote.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage contains several rulings about the effect of structures on the classification of water as kathir or qalil. First, a basin that is 10x10 but has channels (mashari') – if a person performs wudu from one channel and the water is connected to the planks of the channel and not agitated (i.e., the water surface is within the channel and does not move with the rest), it is like a small basin, so wudu is invalid. If the water level is below the planks (i.e., the channel is not submerged, but the water in the basin is separate?), the ruling is different: according to Fath al-Qadir, it is like a large covered basin, so wudu is permissible. The commentator then extends this to a frozen basin: if someone makes a hole and takes water, if the hole is isolated (the water in the hole is separated from the main ice block), it is like a covered basin, so wudu is allowed; if the hole is connected to the main water beneath (e.g., the ice is a layer on top and the water is connected through the hole), it is like a bowl (i.e., the water in the hole is like a small separate basin), so wudu is not allowed. Finally, Fath al-Qadir states that the connection of reeds (in a thicket) does not break the water's connectivity; it remains a great pond, so wudu in thickets is permissible. This illustrates the emphasis on actual water connectivity and agitation for determining kathir status.

Key Terms
مشارع (mashari'): Channels or openings from which water is taken, often in a covered basin
الأجمة (al-ajjam): A thicket of reeds or dense vegetation where water is present but reeds may seem to separate it

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of a frozen large basin, when is it permissible to perform wudu from a hole made in the ice?
A) When the water in the hole is connected to the main water beneath
B) When the water in the hole is separated from the main water (isolated)
C) In all cases
D) In no case

Key Takeaway
Water connectivity, not superficial barriers, determines wudu validity; isolated water, even in large basins, is treated as qalil.

Purification of a Small Basin by Flowing Water
Ruling on purification by inflow of new water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi position on purifying a small basin by inflow and distinguish it from the other two opinions within the school.

Core Idea
Flow-through water purifies immediately—the basin need not be emptied.

When a small basin becomes impure, how do you purify it? The Hanafi school has three opinions, but the preferred view is that as soon as fresh water enters and exits, even in a small amount, the basin becomes pure. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the tarjih.

Guided Path
1
List the three opinions
Identify the three views: (1) immediate purification upon entry and exit; (2) purification after water equal to basin's content exits; (3) after three times that amount exits.
All three opinions are within the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the mufta bihi
According to al-Muhit and others, the first opinion (immediate) is declared correct. This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
Tarjih authority is al-Muhit.
3
Analyze the key condition
Note the condition 'خرج حال دخوله' (exits at the time of entry). This implies a continuous flow-through, not merely adding water without outflow.
Without outflow, the basin may not become pure.
4
Trace the dalil (qiyas)
The ruling is based on qiyas to flowing water: just as a stream purifies itself by carrying impurity away, so does a basin when water flows through it.
The dalil is zanni in both transmission and meaning.
5
Note the extension to wells
Al-Siraj al-Hindi explicitly extends this ruling to wells, showing the principle is general.
The passage cuts off, but the extension is clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو تنجس الحوض الصغير ثم دخل فيه ماء آخر وخرج حال دخوله طهر وإن قل، وقيل لا حتى يخرج قدر ما فيه، وقيل حتى يخرج ثلاثة أمثاله وصحح الأول في المحيط وغيره، قال السراج الهندي وكذا البئر . واعلم أن عبارة كثير منهم في هذه المسألة تفيد أن عن الجمد لا
And if a small basin becomes impure, then other water enters it and exits at the time of entry, it becomes pure even if [the entering water] is little. And it was said: Not until an amount equal to what was in it exits. And it was said: Not until three times its amount exits. The first was declared correct in al-Muhit and others. Al-Siraj al-Hindi said: And likewise the well. And know that the expression of many of them in this issue indicates that regarding ice... [incomplete]
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage addresses the purification of a small basin that has become impure (najis) by the entry of impurity. The method of purification is to flush it with pure water. There are three opinions: (1) It becomes pure as soon as new water enters and exits, even if the amount is small. (2) It becomes pure only after water equal to the original impure water has exited. (3) It becomes pure only after three times the amount has exited. The first opinion (immediate purity upon inflow and outflow) is declared the correct and relied-upon view in al-Muhit and other works. Al-Siraj al-Hindi extends this to wells. The text ends abruptly, mentioning that many scholars' expressions indicate something about ice, but the sentence is incomplete. The key principle is that the flow of water removes impurity, similar to the mechanism of purification in flowing water.

Key Terms
خرج حال دخوله (kharaja hal dukhulihi): Water exits at the same time as the new water enters, implying a flow-through
حوض صغير (hawd saghir): Small basin – a container of water less than 10×10 cubits (approx. 2.25 m per side) in the classical definition

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct view in al-Muhit, when does a small basin that became impure become pure after adding water?
A) Only after all the impure water has been removed
B) As soon as new water enters and exits, even if little
C) Only after three times the volume of water has passed
D) Only after the basin is empty and refilled

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi view is that a small basin becomes pure as soon as new water enters and exits, due to the analogy with flowing water.

Ruling on a Basin When Water Decreases and Re-expands: Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on purity of a re-expanded basin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a large basin when water decreases, and explain the ikhtilaf among later Hanafi scholars on whether re-expansion to 10x10 restores purity, identifying the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
A large basin that decreases becomes like a small one; when it becomes 10x10 again, later Hanafi scholars differed: some say it remains impure, but the preferred view is permissibility.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the Hanafi position on large basins. First, it confirms that a 10x10 basin is not affected by impurity, but if water decreases, it becomes like a small basin such that wudu cannot be performed directly in it. The key dispute arises when the water later re-expands to 10x10: does the basin become pure again? Later scholars disagreed, with al-Siraj al-Hindi preferring the view that it does become pure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial ruling
State the rule for a 10x10 basin: it is pure and wudu is permissible in it.
This is the baseline before any decrease.
2
Note the change when water decreases
When water falls below 10x10, the basin becomes like a small one: one cannot perform wudu in it but can scoop from it.
The act of wudu in the basin is now prohibited.
3
Recognize the specific scenario from al-Khulasa
A basin with an upper part less than 10x10 and a lower part 10x10, where impurity falls or wudu is performed, then water re-expands to 10x10.
This scenario triggers the ikhtilaf.
4
Analyze the ikhtilaf
Later scholars differed; the text provides a detailed answer: if impure water overwhelms the pure at once, the basin is impure; if gradually, it is pure. Some scholars hold it never becomes pure.
The key factor is how the impurity mixes.
5
Conclude with the tarjih
Al-Siraj al-Hindi states the more likely view (ashbah) is permissibility – the basin becomes pure.
This is the mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يجوز التوضؤ فيه والاغتسال فيه، وإن نقص الماء حتى صار أقل من عشرة في عشرة لا يتوضأ فيه ولكن يغترف منه ويتوضأ وفي الخلاصة : ولو كان أعلاه أقل من عشر في عشر وأسفله عشر في عشر ووقعت قطرة خمر أو توضأ منه رجل ثم انتقص الماء وصار عشراً في عشر اختلف المتأخرون فيه، وينبغي أن يكون الجواب على التفصيل: إن كان الماء الذي تنجس في أعلى الحوض أكثر من الماء الذي في أسفله ووقع الماء النجس في الأسفل جملة كان الماء نجساً. ويصير النجس غالباً على الطاهر في وقت واحد، وإن وقع الماء النجس في أسفل الحوض على التدريج كان طاهراً. وقال بعضهم : لا يطهر كالماء القليل إذا وقعت فيه نجاسة ثم انبسط ا هـ . وذكر السراج الهندي أن الأشبه الجواز
It is permissible to perform wudu and ghusl in it. If the water decreases until it becomes less than ten by ten, one should not perform wudu in it but should scoop from it and perform wudu. And in al-Khulasa: If its top is less than ten by ten and its bottom is ten by ten, and a drop of wine falls into it or a man performs wudu from it, then the water decreases and becomes ten by ten, the later scholars differed about it. The answer should be detailed: If the water that became impure in the upper part of the basin is more than the water in its lower part, and the impure water falls into the lower part all at once, the water is impure, and the impurity overwhelms the pure at one time. If the impure water falls into the lower part gradually, it is pure. Some said: it does not become pure, like a small quantity of water when impurity falls into it then it spreads. End. And al-Siraj al-Hindi mentioned that the more likely is permissibility.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about a basin that originally is large (10x10 cubits) but then water decreases. Initially, the basin is large enough that impurity does not affect it (it is like a large pool). But if it decreases below 10x10, it becomes like a small basin: one cannot perform wudu in it directly, but can scoop from it. Then the Khulasa brings a case where the upper part is less than 10x10 but the lower part is 10x10, and impurity falls or someone performs wudu, then water decreases until it becomes 10x10 again. Later scholars differed. The detailed answer: if the impure water in the upper part is more than the pure water in the lower part, and the impure falls all at once, the basin is impure (impurity overwhelms pure at one moment). But if it falls gradually, it is pure. Some (like the author of al-Khulasa?) say it does not become pure, likening it to a small quantity of water that becomes impure and then spreads (i.e., even if it later exceeds 10x10, it remains impure). Al-Siraj al-Hindi preferred permissibility (it becomes pure when it becomes 10x10 again).

Key Terms
عشرة في عشرة (asharat fi asharat): Ten cubits by ten cubits, the standard measurement for a large basin that is not affected by impurity.
الخلاصة (al-Khulasa): A Hanafi fiqh work, likely by al-Imam al-Tahawi or al-Sarakhsi? It is a standard reference text.
الأشبه (al-ashbah): The more likely or preferred view.
التفصيل (al-tafsil): The detailed answer, distinguishing between cases (here: simultaneous vs gradual impurity).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the detailed answer in al-Khulasa, if the impure water in the upper part of a basin is more than the pure water in the lower part and falls all at once, what is the ruling?
A) The basin becomes pure.
B) The basin remains impure.
C) The basin becomes pure only after three changes.
D) The basin becomes pure if the water later becomes 10×10.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prefers that a basin which becomes 10×10 after being small becomes pure again, although some scholars held a stricter view.

Ruling on Wudu from a Large Basin with Outlets
Ruling on wudu from basin outlets with boards

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of wudu from a 10x10 basin with outlets and apply qiyas to determine when water is considered separate.

Core Idea
A large basin with outlets becomes like a small basin if water is connected to boards and not agitated.

We often encounter large water basins with multiple taps or outlets. But does a large size always permit wudu directly? This lesson explores a subtle case: a 10x10 basin with outlets that have boards covering the water. The ruling depends on whether the water is connected to the boards and can move freely. Understanding this helps you apply the principles of water classification correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the baseline ruling for a large basin
A 10x10 basin is considered large (kabir) and normally allows wudu directly, regardless of water movement.
A basin is ‘large’ if its length and width are at least 10 cubits each.
2
Recognize the effect of outlets (mashari‘) with boards
If the water at the outlet is connected to wooden boards (alwah) and does not move (la yadhtarib), it becomes like a small basin. Even if the water level is below the boards, it is still considered roofed (musaqqaf) like a large covered tank.
The boards create effective separation, preventing agitation with the main body.
3
Apply qiyas to the outlet case
Reason by analogy: the outlet resembles a small basin (asl) because water is confined and not agitated. The ruling of a small basin (wudu not permissible directly) is transferred to the outlet.
Illa (effective cause): lack of water movement and effective containment.
4
Extend to similar cases (ice, reeds)
If a large basin freezes and a hole is made, the hole is like an outlet. If water in the hole is disconnected from the main frozen body, it’s permissible (like a roofed basin). If connected, it’s not permissible (like a bowl). Conversely, reeds (qasab) do not break water connection; water in a thicket (ajamah) remains connected, so wudu is permissible.
The key is whether the water is effectively separate and not agitated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي التنجيس: حوض عشر في عشر إلا أن له مشارع فتوضأ رجل من مشرعة أو اغتسل والماء متصل بألواح المشرعة لا يضطرب لا يجوز التوضؤبه وإن كان أسفل من الألواح فإنه لا يجوز، وعلله في فتح القدير بأنه في الأول كالحوض الصغير وفي الثاني حوض كبير مسقف، وعلى هذا الحوض الكبير إذا جمد ماؤه فنقب فيه إنسان نقباً فتوضأ من ذلك الموضع فإن كان الماء منفصلاً بأس به لأنه يصير كالحوض المسقف وإن كان متصلاً لا لأنه صار كالقصعة. كذا في التنجيس وغيره. وفي فتح القدير: واتصال القصب بالقصب لا يمنع اتصال الماء ولا يخرجه عن كونه غديراً عظيماً فيجوز لهذا التوضؤ في الأجمة ونحوها ا هـ. وفي المغرب: الأجمة الشجر الملتف والجمع أجم وآجام وقد قدمنا في الكلام في الفساقي مسألة الأجمة فارجع إليه.
And in al-Tanjis: A basin ten by ten but it has outlets (mashari'), so a man performed wudu from an outlet or bathed, and the water is connected to the boards of the outlet, not agitated, it is not permissible to perform wudu with it. Even if it is below the boards, it is not permissible. It is reasoned in Fath al-Qadir that the first is like a small basin, and the second is like a large roofed basin. And on this, the large basin if its water freezes and a person breaks a hole and performs wudu from that spot: if the water is disconnected, it is okay because it becomes like a roofed basin; if it is connected, it is not because it becomes like a bowl. Similarly in al-Tanjis and others. And in Fath al-Qadir: The connection of reeds to reeds does not prevent the connection of water and does not take it out of being a large pond, so it is permissible to perform wudu in the thicket (ajamah) and the like. End. And in al-Mughrib: al-ajamah is dense trees, plural ajam and ajamin. And we have previously discussed the issue of the thicket in the discussion of fasaqi, so refer to it.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage discusses a 10x10 basin that has multiple small outlets (mashari') like taps or windows. The ruling: if the water is connected to the wooden boards that roof these outlets, and the water does not move when someone draws from it, then each outlet is like a small basin, and wudu is not allowed from it. Even if the water level is below the boards (so that the water is disconnected from the boards), wudu is not allowed because the boards make it like a roofed basin (like a large roofed tank where the water does not move freely). Then a similar case: if a large basin freezes and a hole is made, if the water in the hole is disconnected from the main body, it is like a separate roofed basin and permissible; if connected, it is like a bowl (small). Then the text adds that reeds connected to reeds do not break the connection of water; as long as water is connected, the basin remains like a large pond, so wudu in a thicket (ajamah) is permissible. The author refers to earlier discussion on fasaqi (water channels).

Key Terms
مشارع (mashari'): Plural of mashra'ah, meaning a place where water is drawn, like a spout or tap.
أجمة (ajamah): A thicket of dense trees where water is connected.
ألواح (alwah): Boards, here meaning the wooden covering of an outlet that restrains water movement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it not permissible to perform wudu from an outlet of a 10x10 basin if the water is connected to the boards of the outlet?
A) Because the boards prevent the water from being considered a single large body.
B) Because the water becomes impure by touching the boards.
C) Because the outlet is less than 10x10.
D) Because the outlet is like a separate small basin.

Key Takeaway
Water in a large basin becomes like a small basin if it is restricted by boards and not agitated, making direct wudu invalid.

Small Basin Purification by Inflow and Outflow
Intra-Hanafi dispute on purification criteria

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi opinions on when a small impure basin becomes pure by water flow, and apply the condition of simultaneous outflow.

Core Idea
A small basin becomes pure when water flows in and out simultaneously; the preferred view requires only any outflow, not full replacement.

The purification of a small basin that has become impure is a practical issue in daily taharah. The Hanafi school has an internal difference on the exact condition: does any outflow suffice, or must a full equivalent volume flow out? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines three views and settles on the first, with important nuances about the timing of flow.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and its Legal Context
Recognize that the ruling is about a small basin (less than 10x10 cubits) that has become impure. The question is: when does it become pure again if pure water enters and exits?
The basin is small, so its water is considered non-flowing and thus affected by impurity.
2
List the Three Intra-Hanafi Opinions
From the text, there are three positions: (1) It becomes pure immediately upon any outflow simultaneous with inflow. (2) Not until an amount equal to the basin's water exits. (3) Until three times that amount exits.
The first is said to be 'corrected' (mufta bihi) by later authorities like al-Muhit.
3
Analyze the Preferred View and its Condition
The preferred view requires 'exit at the time of entry' – that is, water must flow out simultaneously as new water flows in. This essentially treats the basin as flowing water in meaning.
If the basin is not full and water only exits after filling, the condition may not be met.
4
Consider the Contemporary Dispute Mentioned
The text also discusses a later difference among teachers: if pure water is poured into a deficient basin until it flows, some consider it not flowing in custom, while others analogize it to a spout (mizab). The author implicitly supports the simultaneous exit condition.
This shows that the ruling is applied to modern situations like jugs or water containers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو تنجس الحوض الصغير ثم دخل فيه ماء آخر وخرج حال دخوله طهر وإن قل، وقيل لا حتى يخرج قدر ما فيه، وقيل حتى يخرج ثلاثة أمثاله وصحح الأول في المحيط وغيره، قال السراج الهندي وكذا البئر . واعلم أن عبارة كثير منهم في هذه المسألة تفيد أن عن الجمد لا قوله : (وفي التنجيس حوض عشر في عشر إلا أن له مشارع هي جمع مشرعة مورد الشاربة . والحاصل أن هذا الحوض مسقف وفيه طاقات لأخذ الماء منه، فإن كان الماء متصلاً بالألواح التي سقف بها هذا الحوض لا يضطرب بالاستعمال لا يجوز التوضؤ منه لأن كل مشرعة منه حينئذ كحوض صغير، وإن كان دون الألواح يجوز لأنه حوض واحد لاضطرابه باستعمال المستعمل منه . قوله: (ولو تنجس الحوض الصغير ثم دخل فيه ماء آخر وخرج (الخ أقول : سيأتي أن الصحيح أنه إذا جرى طهر وإن لم يكن له مدد وسيذكر فروعاً مبنية عليه، وعلى هذا فإذا كان الحوض منتقصاً وتنجس ثم أفرغ فوقه ماء طاهر بنحو قربة حتى جرى ماء الحوض، وكذا الإبريق إذا كان فيه ماء نجس ثم صب فوقه ماء طاهر هل يحكم بطهارته بمجرد ذلك أم لا ؟ ومقتضى ما سيأتي الحكم بطهارته وقد وقع في عصرنا الاختلاف في هذه المسألة بين بعض مشايخنا، فبعضهم منعه مستنداً إلى أنه لا يعد في العرف جارياً، وبعضهم قال يطهر لأنه مثل مسألة الميزاب الآتية حتى أفتى في آنية فيها الحكم بطهارة الحوض إنما هو إذا كان الخروج حالة الدخول وهو كذلك فيما يظهر لأنه حينئذ يكون في المعنى جارياً لكن إياك وظن أنه لو كان الحوض غير ملآن فلم يخرج منه شيء في أول الأمر ثم لما امتلأ خرج منه بعضه لاتصال الماء الجاري به أنه لا يكون طاهراً حينئذ إذ غايته أنه عند إمتلائه قبل خروج الماء منه نجس فيظهر بخروج القدر التعلق به الطهارة إذا اتصل به الماء الجاري الطهور كما لو كان ممتلئاً ابتداء ماء نجساً ثم خرج منه ذلك القدر لاتصال الماء الجاري به ثم كلامهم يشير إلى أن الخارج منه نجس قبل الحكم على الحوض بالطهارة وهو كذلك كما هو ظاهر . كذا في شرح منية المصلي.
And if the small basin becomes impure, then other water enters it and exits at the time of entry, it becomes pure even if it is little. And it is said: not until the amount that is in it exits, and it is said: until three times its amount exits. The first is corrected in al-Muhit and others. Al-Siraj al-Hindi said: and likewise the well. And know that the expression of many of them in this issue indicates that about the ice no? His statement: (And in al-Tanjis: a basin ten by ten but it has outlets, which are the plural of mashra'ah, a watering place. The summary: this basin is roofed and has openings for taking water. If the water is connected to the boards that roof this basin, not agitated by use, it is not permissible to perform wudu from it because each outlet then is like a small basin. And if it is below the boards, it is permissible because it is one basin due to its agitation by the use of the used water. His statement: (And if the small basin becomes impure then other water enters and exits) etc. I say: It will come that the correct view is that if it flows, it becomes pure even if it has no continuous supply, and he will mention branches based on it. And on this, if the basin is deficient and becomes impure, then pure water is poured over it from something like a waterskin until the basin water flows, and similarly the jug if it has impure water and then pure water is poured over it: is it judged pure by that alone or not? The implication of what will come is the ruling of its purity. And in our time there occurred a difference in this issue among some of our teachers. Some prohibited it based on the fact that it is not considered flowing in custom. Some said it becomes pure because it is like the upcoming issue of the spout, until he gave a fatwa about a vessel in which [...] The ruling of the purity of the basin is only when the exit occurs at the time of entry, and that is as it appears because then it is in meaning flowing. But beware of thinking that if the basin is not full, and nothing exits at first, then when it becomes full some of it exits due to connection of flowing water, that it then becomes pure, because at the time of filling before water exits it is impure, then by the exit of that amount connected with it the purity appears if it is connected to pure flowing water, as if it were initially full of impure water then that amount exited due to connection to flowing water. Then their speech indicates that the water that exits is impure before the basin is judged pure, and that is as it is apparent. Similarly in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about purifying a small basin that has become impure. Three opinions: (1) It becomes pure as soon as water enters and exits, even if little exits (chosen in al-Muhit). (2) Not until an amount equal to the basin's content exits. (3) Until three times that amount exits. The first is preferred. The same applies to a well. Then a long commentary discusses details: the condition that exit must be simultaneous with entry; otherwise, if the basin is not full and later water exits after filling, it is not pure until that exiting water is considered. Also includes a difference among contemporary teachers regarding a basin that is deficient and then pure water is poured over it: some say it is not considered flowing in custom, others say it is like the spout case. The author inclines that the exit must be simultaneous with entry for it to be considered flowing in meaning. The text also reiterates that the exiting water is impure until the basin is declared pure.

Key Terms
الحوض الصغير (al-hawd al-saghir): A small basin less than 10x10 cubits, which is affected by impurity.
خرج حال دخوله (kharaja hal dukhulihi): Exit at the time of entry; water must flow out simultaneously as new water enters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) When an amount equal to its content has exited.
B) When three times its content has exited.
C) When water exits at the time of entry, regardless of amount.
D) Only if the incoming water is from a flowing river.

Key Takeaway
A small impure basin becomes pure by flow only when water exits simultaneously with the entry of pure water, and the preferred Hanafi view deems any amount of outflow sufficient.

Ruling on Wudu in a Small Basin with Inflow and Outflow
Explaining the ruling of a small basin with continuous inflow and outflow from different sides

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi fatwa on wudu in a small basin with continuous flow and explain why the ruling is based on the purity of used water and the principle of ghalabat al-zann.

Core Idea
Wudu is permissible from any side of a flowing basin if the water is not strongly suspected to be used.

This passage from Sharh al-Wiqaya and other Hanafi works addresses a practical scenario: a small basin where water flows in from one side and out from another. Scholars debated whether wudu could be performed from all sides or only at the exit point. The chosen fatwa permits it from all sides, based on the purity of used water and reliance on preponderance of opinion rather than exact measurements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing wudu (ablution) from a small basin with water entering from one side and exiting from another. The ruling is that it is permissible (yajuz) to perform wudu from all its sides, regardless of the basin's size.
This is the mufta bihi position according to the cited authorities.
2
Locate the basis of the disagreement
The disagreement among Hanafi scholars over this issue stems from the status of used water (ma' musta'mal). Those who consider used water impure (najis) restrict wudu to the exit point to avoid using contaminated water. The chosen view holds used water is pure (tahir), so no such restriction applies.
The purity of used water is the foundational qaw'id behind the ruling.
3
Understand the condition for permissibility
Even with the chosen view, wudu is not absolutely permitted. The person must not have a strong presumption (ghalabat al-zann) that the water he scoops contains used water or that half or more of the water he uses is used.
This condition is derived from later fatwa sources like Fath al-Qadir.
4
Recognize the methodological shift from measurement to approximation
Earlier rulings often relied on exact measurements (e.g., a basin of 10x10 cubits) to ensure purity. The later chosen view replaces these measurements with the concept of 'much' or 'large' based on customary perception (ghalabat al-zann), making the ruling practical.
This shift is explicitly stated at the end of the passage: 'in every issue, the word 'ten' is replaced by 'much' or 'large'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي شرح الوقاية : وإذا كان حوض صغير يدخل فيه الماء من جانب ويخرج من جانب يجوز الوضوء في جميع جوانبه وعليه الفتوى من غير تفصيل بين أن يكون أربعاً في أربع أو أقل فيجوز، أو أكثر فلا يجوز. وفي معراج الدراية : يفتي بالجواز مطلقاً والمتمده في فتاوى قاضيخان. وفي فتح القدير : إن الخلاف مبني على نجاسة الماء المستعمل فقولهم في هذه المسألة أنه لا يجوز الوضوء إلا في موضع خروج الماء إنما هو بناء على نجاسة الماء المستعمل وأما على المختار من طهارة الماء المستعمل فالجواب في هذه المسألة كما تقدم في نظائرها أنه يجوز الوضوء فيها ما لم يغلب على ظن المتوضىء أن ما يغترفه لإسقاط فرض ماء مستعمل أو ما يخالطه منه مقدار نصفه فصاعداً، فكن على هذا معتمداً. كذا في شرح منية المصلي للعلامة ابن أمير حاج رحمه الله تعالى. واعلم أن أكثر التفاريع المذكورة في الكتب مبنية على اعتبار العشر في العشر، فأما على المختار من اعتبار غلبة الظن فيوضع مكان لفظ عشر في كل مسألة لفظ كثير أو كبير ثم تجري التفاريع ا هـ.
And in Sharh al-Wiqaya: If there is a small basin into which water enters from one side and exits from another, it is permissible to perform wudu from all its sides, and on this is the fatwa without distinction between it being four by four or less (it is permissible) or more (it is not permissible). And in Mi'raj al-Diraya: He gives a fatwa of permissibility absolutely, and the formal opinion in Fatawa Qadikhan. And in Fath al-Qadir: Indeed the disagreement is based on the impurity of used water. Their statement in this issue that wudu is not permissible except at the place of water exit is only based on the impurity of used water. As for the chosen view of the purity of used water, the answer in this issue is as presented in similar cases: it is permissible to perform wudu in it as long as the person performing wudu does not strongly think that what he scoops for the obligation is used water or that mixed with it is half or more. So rely on this. Similarly in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli by Allamah Ibn Amir Haj, may Allah have mercy on him. And know that most of the branches mentioned in the books are based on the consideration of ten by ten. As for the chosen view of considering preponderance of opinion (ghalabat al-zann), instead of the word 'ten', in every issue the word 'much' or 'large' is placed, then the branches proceed accordingly. End.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage gives the fatwa on a small basin with water flowing in from one side and out from another. The ruling: wudu is permissible from all sides of the basin, regardless of the size (even if less than 4x4). This is based on the view that used water is pure (tahir), not impure. If used water were considered impure, wudu would only be allowed at the exit point. But the chosen view (mukhtar) is that used water is pure, so wudu is allowed from anywhere in the basin, as long as the person does not have strong suspicion that the water he is using is used water or contains half or more used water. The author notes that many rulings in books are based on the 10x10 measurement, but the chosen view is to rely on general perception of largeness rather than exact dimensions. So in each case, replace 'ten' with 'much' or 'large'.

Key Terms
ماء مستعمل (ma' musta'mal): Water that has been used for ablution (wudu or ghusl).
غلبة الظن (ghalabat al-zann): Preponderance of opinion or strong presumption; the standard for determining whether water is pure.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only at the point where water enters.
B) Only at the point where water exits.
C) From all sides, regardless of size.
D) Only if the basin is 4x4 or larger.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi fatwa permits wudu from all sides of a flowing basin, based on the purity of used water and reliance on ghalabat al-zann over strict measurements.

Purity of Non-Water Liquids and Purification by Flow
Discussing the proof of Imam Malik and applying basin rulings to other liquids and vessels

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that non-water liquids are ruled like water in purity, compare it with Imam Malik's proof, and apply the principle of flow to purify vessels and basins.

Core Idea
Non-water liquids follow water's purity rules: flow purifies them, but this extension is disputed.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq transitions from detailing branches (furu') to presenting proofs (dalil). It first confirms that all pure liquids (like rose water, oils) are governed by the same rules as water regarding impurity: if the quantity is small, impurity affects it; if large, it does not. The core dispute arises when applying the principle of purification by flow to these liquids. Imam Malik's proof from a hadith forms the basis, and the text extends this to bathhouse basins and vessels, concluding that flow (even minimal entry and exit of water) renders them pure. However, the extension to all liquids was contested by later scholars.

Guided Path
1
State the general principle for non-water liquids
Identify that the author says all other liquids (mā'i'āt) are like water in terms of small and large quantities: if a small amount gets impurity, it becomes impure; if large (like a well), it remains pure unless changed.
The principle is qiyas (analogy) to water.
2
Analyze Imam Malik's proof
Examine the hadith quoted: 'Pure water is not made impure by anything except that which changes its taste.' This is cited as a proof (dalīl). Consider its transmission (ahad) and implication: that impurity only matters if it alters the water.
The hadith is used to argue that flow can remove impurity, but it explicitly mentions water only.
3
Extend to rose water and other liquids
Note the author's discussion: if rose water becomes impure and then pure water or pure rose water is poured over it, causing flow, it becomes pure. This applies by analogy (qiyas) to water, but only if the added liquid is pure.
The author mentions that some Hanafis in Aleppo extended this to all liquids, but they were criticized.
4
Understand the basin and vessel ruling
From al-Bada'i', the passage states that a bathhouse basin (hawd al-hammam) or vessels become pure simply by the entry and exit of water, even a small amount, because it becomes flowing water and certainty of remaining impurity is gone.
This is based on the correct opinion (al-qawl al-sahīh) among the three opinions for a small basin.
5
Reflect on the methodological lesson
Consider why later scholars rejected the blanket extension to all liquids: the proof explicitly mentions water, and qiyas may be weak if the illa (effective cause) is not identical. The author encourages reflection (tata'ammal).
This shows the tension between text (nass) and analogy (qiyas) in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسائر المائعات كالماء في القلة والكثرة يعني كل مقدار لو كان ماء تنجس فإذا كان غيره ينجس . وحيث انتهينا من التفاريع المذكورة في الكتب نرجع إلى بيان الدلائل للأئمة فنقول : استدل الإمام مالك رضي الله عنه بقوله الماء الطهور لا ينجسه شيء إلا ما غير طعمه ماء ورد وقعت فيها نجاسة بأنها تطهر بمجرد جريانها بأن يصب فوقها ماء قراح أو ماء ورد طاهر أخذاً مما ذكر. ومما سيأتي قريباً أن سائر المائعات كالماء لكن أخبرنا شيخنا حفظه الله تعالى أن بعض أهل عصره في حلب أفتى بذلك أيضاً في المائعات فأقام عليه النكير أهل عصره ولم يقبلوا ذلك منه فتأمل. قلت: ورأيت في البدائع بعد ذكر الخلاف في تطهير الحوض الصغير من الأقوال الثلاثة المذكورة في كلام المؤلف قال ما نصه : وعلى هذا حوض الحمام أو الأواني إذا تنجست اهـ. ومقتضاه طهارة الأواني بمجرد دخول الماء وخروجه وإن قل بناء على القول الصحيح من الأقوال الثلاثة، وأنه يعد جارياً، وقد علل في البدائع هذا القول بقوله لأنه صار ماء جارياً ولم نستيقن ببقاء النجاسة فيه . أخذ الفقيه أبو الليث قوله : (ثم) كلامهم الخ إذا قلنا أنه لا يطهر ما لم يخرج قدر ما فيه قال وبه
And all other liquids are like water in smallness and largeness, meaning every quantity: if it were water and became impure, then if it is other than water it becomes impure. And since we have finished from the branches mentioned in the books, we return to explaining the proofs for the imams. We say: Imam Malik, may Allah be pleased with him, argued with his statement: 'Pure water is not made impure by anything except that which changes its taste.' Rose water in which impurity has fallen becomes pure merely by its flow, by pouring over it pure water or pure rose water, taking from what was mentioned. And from what will come shortly, that all liquids are like water, but our teacher (may Allah preserve him) informed us that some of his contemporaries in Aleppo gave a fatwa to that effect also for liquids, so the people of his time criticized him and did not accept that from him, so reflect. I said: And I saw in al-Bada'i' after mentioning the difference in purifying the small basin from the three opinions mentioned in the author's words, he said in his text: 'And upon this is the bathhouse basin or vessels when they become impure.' End. And its implication is the purity of vessels merely by the entry and exit of water, even if little, based on the correct of the three opinions, and that it is considered flowing. And he gave the reason in al-Bada'i' for this view by saying: 'Because it becomes flowing water and we are not certain of the remaining impurity in it.' The jurist Abu al-Layth took his statement: 'Then their words etc.' if we say that it does not become pure until the amount in it exits, he said: and with it...
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage transitions from the branches (furu') to the proofs (dalil). It first states that other liquids (like oils, rose water) follow the same rules as water in terms of small and large quantities: if the liquid is small, impurity affects it; if large, it does not. Then it mentions Imam Malik's proof from a hadith that water is not impure unless changed. The text then discusses rose water: if rose water becomes impure and then more pure water or pure rose water is poured over it so that it flows, it becomes pure. The author notes that some later scholars extended this to all liquids, but they were criticized. Then from al-Bada'i', the author quotes that the same ruling as for a small basin (the three opinions) applies to a bathhouse basin and vessels: they become pure by the mere entry and exit of water, based on the correct opinion that flowing water purifies. This is because it becomes flowing water and we are not certain of remaining impurity. Finally, there is a note from Abu al-Layth about the opinion requiring outflow of the basin's content.

Key Terms
ماء ورد (ma' ward): Rose water, a liquid other than water (mā' ghayr mutlaq).
حوض الحمام (hawd al-hammam): The basin in a bathhouse often fed by flowing water.
مائعات (mā'i'āt): Liquids (plural of mā'i').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage from al-Bada'i', how does a bathhouse basin become pure after impurity?
A) Only if it is completely emptied and refilled three times.
B) By the entry and exit of water, even if little, because it becomes flowing.
C) Only if the water in it is changed three times.
D) It cannot be purified because it is not flowing.

Key Takeaway
Non-water pure liquids are analogous to water in impurity rulings, but the extension of purification by flow to all liquids is disputed; the basin and vessels are purified by flow because they become flowing water.

intermediate
8 min
Ruling on Purifying a Small Basin with Flowing Water
States Hanafi ruling on purity of a small basin with flowing water and analogizes other liquids.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a small basin (hawd saghir) becomes pure through flowing water and apply the principle of predominant doubt (ghalabat al-zann) to determine impurity.

Core Idea
A small basin becomes pure only when its water is fully displaced by flowing water; reliance on strict measures is replaced by predominant doubt.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on the purification of a small basin connected to flowing water, a common scenario in wudu facilities. The text clarifies misconceptions about when the basin is considered pure and introduces the critical methodological shift from fixed numerical limits to the criterion of predominant doubt (ghalabat al-zann). Understanding this ruling helps you correctly assess the purity of water in continuous-flow systems and other liquids.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Basin's Condition
The author states that a basin is ruled pure only if water exits at the time of entry, making it effectively flowing (jari). This is the key condition for purification. Determine whether the basin's water is flowing or still.
Flowing water (al-ma' al-jari) purifies itself and also purifies the basin it passes through.
2
Analyze the Counterexample
Consider a basin initially empty: as water flows in, no water exits until the basin fills. During filling, the basin is impure because the incoming water mixes with any residual impurity (or the water itself is considered impure until the basin is fully flushed). Purity is established only after the initial water has been displaced and fresh water flows out.
The water that first exits is impure until the basin is ruled pure.
3
Differentiate Between the Strict and Chosen Positions
Earlier Hanafi texts relied on a strict numerical ratio (e.g., ten in ten) to determine impurity. The chosen position (mufta bihi) replaces this with ghalabat al-zann (predominant doubt). The student must understand that numerical measures are no longer operative; instead, one assesses whether the water appears 'much' or 'large' relative to the impurity.
Ghalabat al-zann is a subjective threshold determined by the reasonable person.
4
Extend the Ruling to Other Liquids
The passage concludes that other liquids (oils, milk, etc.) follow the same rule: if a small amount would make water impure, the same applies to them. This is based on qiyas (analogy). The student must apply the same condition of 'flowing' and predominant doubt to other liquids.
This ensures consistent methodology across different substances.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحكم بطهارة الحوض إنما هو إذا كان الخروج حالة الدخول وهو كذلك فيما يظهر لأنه حينئذ يكون في المعنى جارياً لكن إياك وظن أنه لو كان الحوض غير ملآن فلم يخرج منه شيء في أول الأمر ثم لما امتلأ خرج منه بعضه لاتصال الماء الجاري به أنه لا يكون طاهراً حينئذ إذ غايته أنه عند إمتلائه قبل خروج الماء منه نجس فيظهر بخروج القدر التعلق به الطهارة إذا اتصل به الماء الجاري الطهور كما لو كان ممتلئاً ابتداء ماء نجساً ثم خرج منه ذلك القدر لاتصال الماء الجاري به ثم كلامهم يشير إلى أن الخارج منه نجس قبل الحكم على الحوض بالطهارة وهو كذلك كما هو ظاهر . كذا في شرح منية المصلي. وفي شرح الوقاية : وإذا كان حوض صغير يدخل فيه الماء من جانب ويخرج من جانب يجوز الوضوء في جميع جوانبه وعليه الفتوى من غير تفصيل بين أن يكون أربعاً في أربع أو أقل فيجوز، أو أكثر فلا يجوز. وفي معراج الدراية : يفتي بالجواز مطلقاً والمتمده في فتاوى قاضيخان. وفي فتح القدير : إن الخلاف مبني على نجاسة الماء المستعمل فقولهم في هذه المسألة أنه لا يجوز الوضوء إلا في موضع خروج الماء إنما هو بناء على نجاسة الماء المستعمل وأما على المختار من طهارة الماء المستعمل فالجواب في هذه المسألة كما تقدم في نظائرها أنه يجوز الوضوء فيها ما لم يغلب على ظن المتوضىء أن ما يغترفه لإسقاط فرض ماء مستعمل أو ما يخالطه منه مقدار نصفه فصاعداً، فكن على هذا معتمداً. كذا في شرح منية المصلي للعلامة ابن أمير حاج رحمه الله تعالى. واعلم أن أكثر التفاريع المذكورة في الكتب مبنية على اعتبار العشر في العشر، فأما على المختار من اعتبار غلبة الظن فيوضع مكان لفظ عشر في كل مسألة لفظ كثير أو كبير ثم تجري التفاريع ا هـ. وسائر المائعات كالماء في القلة والكثرة يعني كل مقدار لو كان ماء تنجس فإذا كان غيره ينجس .
The ruling on the purification of the basin is only when the water exits at the time of entry, and it is so in what appears, because then it is in meaning flowing. But beware of thinking that if the basin was not full and nothing came out of it initially, then when it became full some of it came out due to the connection of flowing water, that it would not be pure then. For its utmost is that at the time of filling before the water comes out of it, it is impure; then with the exit of that amount, purity becomes attached to it if the flowing purifying water connects to it, just as if it was initially full of impure water then that amount came out due to the connection of flowing water. Then their words indicate that what comes out of it is impure before ruling on the basin as pure, and it is so as is apparent. Thus in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli. And in Sharh al-Wiqaya: If there is a small basin into which water enters from one side and exits from another, it is permissible to perform wudu in all its sides, and upon this is the fatwa without distinction between whether it is four by four or less, then it is permissible, or more, then it is not permissible. And in Mi'raj al-Diraya: Fatwa is given for permissibility absolutely, and it is preferred in Fatawa Qadi Khan. And in Fath al-Qadir: The difference of opinion is based on the impurity of used water; their statement in this matter that wudu is not permissible except at the place of water exit is based on the impurity of used water. As for the chosen position of purity of used water, the answer in this matter is as presented in its parallels: that wudu in it is permissible as long as it does not dominate the thought of the one performing wudu that what he scoops to fulfill an obligatory act is used water, or that mixed with it is half or more of used water. So rely on this. Thus in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli by allamah Ibn Amir Hajj, may Allah have mercy on him. And know that most of the detailed rulings mentioned in books are based on considering the ten in a ten; but as for the chosen position of considering predominant doubt, the word 'ten' is replaced in every issue with the word 'much' or 'large', then the details proceed. End. And other liquids are like water in scarcity and abundance, meaning every amount that, if it were water, would become impure, then if it is other than water, it becomes impure.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the Hanafi school regarding the purification of a small basin (hawd saghir) connected to flowing water. The author begins by stating that a basin is considered pure when water flows in and out simultaneously, as it becomes effectively flowing water. He warns against a mistaken assumption: if the basin is initially empty, water enters but does not exit until it fills, then the basin is impure until the original water is displaced and purity is established by the flowing water. The water that exits before the basin is ruled pure is itself impure. The passage then quotes several authoritative Hanafi commentaries: Sharh Munyat al-Musalli, Sharh al-Wiqaya (where wudu is permissible in all parts of the basin regardless of dimensions, and this is the fatwa), Mi'raj al-Diraya (absolutely permissible), and Fath al-Qadir (which relates the difference to the impurity of used water; on the chosen view that used water is pure, wudu is allowed unless the user predominantly doubts that the water he uses is used water or half of it is such). The author then notes a key methodological point: most detailed rulings in books assume a strict numeric ratio ('ashr fi 'ashr), but the chosen position replaces 'ten' with 'much' or 'large', relying on predominant doubt (ghalabat al-zann). Finally, the passage states that other liquids (such as milk and oils) follow the same rule as water regarding impurity: if a small amount of impurity would make water impure, the same applies to other liquids. This is a concise summary of the Hanafi position on mixed liquids.

Key Terms
حوض صغير (hawd saghir): A small basin or pool, typically used for wudu, with continuous inflow and outflow of water.
غلبة الظن (ghalabat al-zann): Predominant doubt; a subjective criterion replacing strict numerical measures in determining impurity.
مستعمل (musta'mal): Used water, i.e., water that has already been used for wudu or ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
On the chosen Hanafi position (mufta bihi), what criterion replaces the strict numerical ratio ('ashr fi 'ashr) for determining impurity in a small basin?
A) The basin must be 4x4 cubits.
B) The user must have predominant doubt (ghalabat al-zann) that the water is heavily contaminated.
C) The water must be used for wudu at the exit point.
D) The basin must have a volume of exactly 20 cubic cubits.

Key Takeaway
A small basin with flowing water becomes pure only when the original water is displaced, and the mufta bihi ruling relies on predominant doubt rather than fixed measures, extending analogously to all liquids.

The Inter-Madhhab Dispute on Water Impurity
Presents and responds to proofs from three imams on water impurity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three madhhab positions on water impurity, identify their primary proofs, and explain why the Hanafi school does not accept the qullatan threshold.

Core Idea
Water impurity is determined by contact, not volume — the Hanafi position relies on the general Quranic prohibition without exception.

This passage from Sharh Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents the proofs of the three great Imams regarding the ruling on water when it comes into contact with impurity. It contrasts the Maliki, Shafi'i, and Hanafi positions and ultimately upholds the Hanafi view. The author first cites Imam Malik's proof that water remains pure unless its properties change, then moves to Shafi'i's proof based on the two-qulla hadith, and finally presents Abu Hanifa's proof from the Quranic verse prohibiting khaba'ith and supporting hadiths. The Hanafi response to the other proofs is given, establishing the school's relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Articulate the Hanafi ruling: water becomes impure (najis) upon any contact with impurity, regardless of volume or change in properties.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opposing schools and their views
State the Maliki position (water remains pure unless properties change) and the Shafi'i position (water remains pure if it reaches two qullas and shows no change).
Both opponents allow exceptions based on volume or change.
3
Analyze the opponent's primary proof
For Malik: 'Water is pure unless changed' – criterion of change. For Shafi'i: 'If water reaches two qullas, it does not carry impurity' – quantitative threshold.
The author quotes part of Malik's proof in the Arabic text.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds that the Quranic verse on khaba'ith is general and unrestricted; the two-qulla hadith is not definitively proven and contradicts stronger evidence. The hadith of urinating in still water shows that even a small impurity suffices.
The Hanafi response is rooted in usul: amm cannot be restricted by a zanni text.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: For a large water tank, Hanafi says it becomes impure with any drop of impurity; Shafi'i says it remains pure if it is over two qullas and unchanged. This affects rulings on wudu and ghusl.
The thamarah is the real-world application of the dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحيث انتهينا من التفاريع المذكورة في الكتب نرجع إلى بيان الدلائل للأئمة فنقول : استدل الإمام مالك رضي الله عنه بقوله الماء الطهور لا ينجسه شيء إلا ما غير طعمه ماء ورد وقعت فيها نجاسة بأنها تطهر بمجرد جريانها بأن يصب فوقها ماء قراح أو ماء ورد طاهر أخذاً مما ذكر. ومما سيأتي قريباً أن سائر المائعات كالماء لكن أخبرنا شيخنا حفظه الله تعالى أن بعض أهل عصره في حلب أفتى بذلك أيضاً في المائعات فأقام عليه النكير أهل عصره ولم يقبلوا ذلك منه فتأمل. قلت: ورأيت في البدائع بعد ذكر الخلاف في تطهير الحوض الصغير من الأقوال الثلاثة المذكورة في كلام المؤلف قال ما نصه : وعلى هذا حوض الحمام أو الأواني إذا تنجست اهـ. ومقتضاه طهارة الأواني بمجرد دخول الماء وخروجه وإن قل بناء على القول الصحيح من الأقوال الثلاثة، وأنه يعد جارياً، وقد علل في البدائع هذا القول بقوله لأنه صار ماء جارياً ولم نستيقن ببقاء النجاسة فيه . أخذ الفقيه أبو الليث قوله : (ثم) كلامهم الخ أي إذا قلنا أنه لا يطهر ما لم يخرج قدر ما فيه
And since we have finished with the detailed rulings mentioned in the books, we return to the explanation of the proofs for the Imams. We say: Imam Malik, may Allah be pleased with him, argued by his statement: 'The purifying water is not impurified by anything except what changes its taste.' [He argued about] rose water in which impurity fell, that it becomes purified by its mere flow, by pouring over it clear water or pure rose water, taking from what was mentioned. And from what will come soon is that other liquids are like water. But our shaykh, may Allah protect him, told us that some of his contemporaries in Aleppo gave a fatwa to that effect also regarding liquids, so the people of his time criticized him and did not accept that from him, so reflect. I said: And I saw in al-Bada'i after mentioning the difference of opinion on purifying the small basin, from the three statements mentioned in the author's speech, he said, verbatim: 'And upon this is the basin of the bathhouse or utensils if they become impure...' End. And its implication is the purity of utensils merely by the entry and exit of water, even if little, based on the correct of the three statements, and that it is considered flowing. And in al-Bada'i he gave as a reason for this statement: because it becomes flowing water and we are not certain of the continuation of impurity in it. The faqih Abu al-Layth took his statement: (Then) their speech etc., meaning if we say that it is not purified until the amount in it exits.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute where the author presents the proofs of the three Imams regarding the impurity of water. He begins with Imam Malik's proof: water is pure unless its taste, color, or smell changes. Malik uses the example of rose water with impurity—it becomes pure by flowing clear water over it. The author then notes a related contemporary fatwa in Aleppo applying the same rule to other liquids, but it was not accepted. He then quotes from al-Bada'i regarding the small basin, saying that even utensils in a bathhouse become pure by mere entry and exit of water, based on the correct view that it is considered flowing water. The passage then continues on page 144 with Imam Shafi'i's proof using the hadith 'If water reaches two qullas, it does not carry impurity' and Imam Abu Hanifa's proof using the Quranic verse 'And prohibits for them the impure things' (7:157) and various hadiths, concluding that the Hanafi position is that water becomes impure with any contact with impurity, regardless of quantity or change. The passage ends with the hadith references cited by the author.

Key Terms
قلتان (qullatan): Two qullas, a measure of water volume used by Imam Shafi'i as a threshold for water purity.
خبث (khabath): Impurity; used in the hadith 'لا يحمل خبثاً' meaning impurity.
ماء طهور (ma' tahur): Purifying water, i.e., water that is both pure and purifying for others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position presented in the lesson, what is the basis for water becoming impure?
A) Only if the water changes in taste, color, or smell.
B) Only if the water is less than two qullas.
C) Any contact with impurity, as derived from the Quranic prohibition of impure things.
D) Only if the impurity is visible.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, water becomes impure by mere contact with impurity, regardless of volume or change, based on the general Quranic prohibition of khaba'ith and supporting hadiths.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate

Dispute on Impure Water: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Debate between Hanafi and Shafi'i over the quantity of water that prevents impurity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state both the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on water impurity, identify their primary proofs, and explain the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of the disagreement.

Core Idea
No quantity of water is safe from impurity in the Hanafi school — the Shafi'i two-qullah threshold is rejected.

The purity of water is a foundational issue in Islamic law, affecting daily worship. This lesson examines a key disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam al-Shafi'i: does a large body of water (two qullahs or more) remain pure after contact with an impurity, unless its qualities change? We will explore the proofs each school presents and understand the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
First, clearly articulate the Hanafi ruling: any water becomes impure upon contact with impurity, regardless of quantity or whether its properties change.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that water reaching two qullahs (approx. 200 liters) does not become impure unless its color, taste, or smell changes. His primary evidence is the hadith: 'When water reaches two qullahs, it does not carry impurity.'
3
Follow the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof
Abu Hanifa argues that this hadith is not definitive, and he presents alternative evidence from the Quran (al-A'raf: 157), other hadiths (about stagnant water, washing hands, dog's lapping), and qiyas with other liquids.
Notice the Hanafi reliance on general principles and multiple evidences.
4
Analyze the Hanafi dalil chain
Examine how the Hanafi proofs collectively establish that impurity renders water impure without exception. The Quranic verse prohibits 'al-khaba'ith' absolutely, and the other hadiths show prohibition even without observable change.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The difference is practical: Hanafis must avoid any water with certain or strong presumption of impurity, while Shafi'is only deem it impure if the quantity is less than two qullahs or if properties change. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq upholds the Hanafi position.
This affects daily use, e.g., swimming pools or large tanks.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو لونه أو ريحه (۱) واستدل الإمام الشافعي رضي الله عنه بقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم «إذا بلغ الماء قلتين لا يحمل خبثاً» (۲) واستدل أبو حنيفة على ما ذكره الرازي في أحكام القرآن بقوله تعالى ويحرم عليهم الخبائث [الأعراف : ١٥٧] والنجاسات لا محالة من الخبائث فحرمها الله تحريماً مبهماً ولم يفرق بين حال اختلاطها وانفرادها بالماء فوجب تحريم استعمال كل ما تيقنا به جزءاً من النجاسة، وتكون جهة الخطر من طريق النجاسة أولى من جهة الإباحة لأن الأصل أنه إذا اجتمع المحرم والمبيح قدم المحرم وأيضاً لا نعلم بين الفقهاء في سائر المائعات إذا خالطه اليسير من النجاسة كاللبن والأدهان أن حكم اليسير في ذلك كحكم الكثير وأنه محظور عليه أكل ذلك وشربه، فكذا الماء بجامع لزوم اجتناب النجاسات ويدل عليه من السنة قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم «لا يبولن أحدكم في الماء الدائم ثم يغتسل فيه من «الجنابة وفي لفظ آخر «ولا يغتسلن فيه من جنابة»، ومعلوم أن البول القليل في الماء الكثير لا يغير لونه ولا طعمه ولا رائحته وقد منع منه النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ، ويدل عليه أيضاً قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا استيقظ أحدكم من منامه فليغسل يده ثلاثاً قبل أن يدخلها الإناء فإنه لا يدري أين باتت يده (۳) فأمر بغسل اليد احتياطاً أصابته من موضع الاستنجاء، ومعلوم أنها لا تغير الماء ولولا أنها مفسدة عند التحقيق لما كان للأمر بالاحتياط معنى وحكم النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بنجاسة ولوغ الكلب بقوله «طهور إناء أحدكم إذا ولغ فيه الكلب أن يغسل سبعاً»(٤) وهو لا يغير ا هـ. فالحاصل أنه حيث غلب على الظن وجود نجاسة في الماء لا يجوز استعماله أصلاً بهذه الدلائل لا فرق بين أن يكون قلتين أو أكثر أو أقل، تغير أو لا. وهذا مذهب أبي حنيفة والتقدير بشيء دون شيء لا بد فيه من نص ولم يوجد، وفي بعض هذا الاستدلال كلام نذكره إن شاء الله تعالى. وأما ما استدل به من نجاسة مالك أو ثلاثة أمثاله فذلك الخارج قبل بلوغه القدر المذكور نجس لأنه لم يحكم بطهارة الحوض، فكذا ما خرج منه بخلاف ما إذا قلنا بطهارته بمجرد الخروج فإن ذلك الخارج طاهر لحكمنا بطهارة الحوض (۱) رواه أبو داود في كتاب الطهارة باب ٣٤ الترمذي في كتاب الطهارة باب ٤٩. النسائي في كتاب المياه باب ۲،۱. أحمد في مسنده (٢٣٥/١، ٢٨٤). (۲) رواه أبو داود في كتاب الطهارة باب ۳۳ الترمذي في كتاب الطهارة باب ٥٠. النسائي في كتاب الطهارة باب ٤٣. أحمد في مسنده (۱۲/۲، ۳۸). (۳) رواه البخاري في كتاب الوضوء باب ٢٦ مسلم في كتاب الطهارة حديث ۸۷، ۸۸. أبو داود في كتاب الطهارة باب ٤٩ الترمذي في كتاب الطهارة باب .۱۹ أحمد في مسنده (٢٤١/٢). (4) رواه البخاري في كتاب الوضوء باب ۳۳ مسلم في كتاب الطهارة حديث ٨٩. أبو داود في كتاب الطهارة باب ۳۷ الترمذي في كتاب الطهارة باب ٦٨ النسائي في كتاب الطهارة باب ابن ماجه في كتاب الطهارة باب .۳۱ أحمد في مسنده (٢٤٥/٢، ٢٥٣). .٥٠ ٥٢
Or its color or smell. (1) Imam al-Shafi'i, may Allah be pleased with him, argued with his statement, peace be upon him: 'When water reaches two qullahs, it does not carry impurity.' (2) Abu Hanifa argued, as al-Razi mentioned in Ahkam al-Quran, with the statement of Allah Almighty: 'And He makes unlawful for them the impure things' [al-A'raf: 157]. And impurities are undoubtedly among the impure things. So Allah prohibited them with an absolute prohibition and did not distinguish between the state of their mixing with water and their isolation from it. Thus, it becomes obligatory to prohibit the use of every [water] in which we are certain a part of impurity exists. And the aspect of danger from the direction of impurity takes precedence over the aspect of permissibility because the principle is that when the forbidden and the permitted are combined, the forbidden is given precedence. Also, we do not know among the jurists regarding other liquids, if a small amount of impurity mixes with them like milk and oils, that the ruling of the small amount is like the ruling of the large amount and that it is prohibited to eat and drink that. So too with water, due to the common cause of the necessity of avoiding impurities. And evidence from the Sunnah is his statement, peace be upon him: 'Let none of you urinate in stagnant water then bathe in it from janabah.' And in another wording: 'Let him not bathe in it from janabah.' And it is known that a small amount of urine in a large amount of water does not change its color, taste, or smell, yet the Prophet, peace be upon him, prohibited from it. And also evidence is his statement, peace be upon him: 'When one of you wakes from his sleep, let him wash his hand three times before putting it into the vessel, for he does not know where his hand spent the night.' (3) So he ordered washing the hand as a precaution because it touched the place of istinja', and it is known that it does not change the water. And if it were not corrupting in reality, the order of precaution would have no meaning. And the Prophet, peace be upon him, ruled on the impurity of the dog's lapping with his statement: 'The purification of the vessel of one of you when a dog laps from it is to wash it seven times.' (4) And it [the lapping] does not change it. End quote. The conclusion is that wherever there is a preponderant assumption of the presence of impurity in water, it is not permissible to use it at all, based on these evidences. No difference whether it is two qullahs or more or less, changed or not. This is the madhhab of Abu Hanifa. And estimation by a specific measure without any proof requires textual evidence, and none exists. In some of this argumentation there is discussion we will mention if Allah wills. As for what was argued with from the impurity of Malik or three times its like: that which exits before reaching the mentioned amount is impure because we did not rule the trough to be pure. So too what exits from it, contrary to if we ruled it pure merely by exiting, then that exiting [water] would be pure because we ruled the trough pure. (1) Reported by Abu Dawud in the Book of Taharah, Chapter 34; al-Tirmidhi in the Book of Taharah, Chapter 49; al-Nasa'i in the Book of Waters, Chapters 1,2; Ahmad in his Musnad (1/235, 284). (2) Reported by Abu Dawud in the Book of Taharah, Chapter 33; al-Tirmidhi in the Book of Taharah, Chapter 50; al-Nasa'i in the Book of Taharah, Chapter 43; Ahmad in his Musnad (2/12, 38). (3) Reported by al-Bukhari in the Book of Wudu', Chapter 26; Muslim in the Book of Taharah, Hadith 87,88; Abu Dawud in the Book of Taharah, Chapter 49; al-Tirmidhi in the Book of Taharah, Chapter 19; Ahmad in his Musnad (2/241). (4) Reported by al-Bukhari in the Book of Wudu', Chapter 33; Muslim in the Book of Taharah, Hadith 89; Abu Dawud in the Book of Taharah, Chapter 37; al-Tirmidhi in the Book of Taharah, Chapter 68; al-Nasa'i in the Book of Taharah, Chapter 50; Ibn Majah in the Book of Taharah, Chapter 31; Ahmad in his Musnad (2/245, 253).
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the effect of impurity on water. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, explaining Kanz al-Daqa'iq, presents the arguments. Al-Shafi'i relies on the hadith 'When water reaches two qullahs, it does not carry impurity,' meaning that large quantities of water (approximately 200 liters) are not rendered impure by contact with impurity unless one of its three qualities (color, taste, smell) changes. Abu Hanifa, on the other hand, argues that any quantity of water becomes impure upon contact with impurity, regardless of size or change. His evidence includes: (1) The Quranic verse that prohibits impure things, which applies absolutely without distinction between mixing and isolation. (2) The principle that when the forbidden and permitted conflict, the forbidden prevails. (3) Qiyas (analogy) with other liquids like milk and oil, where even a small impurity renders the whole mixture prohibited. (4) The hadith forbidding urination in stagnant water, which applies even though a small amount of urine does not change the water's properties. (5) The hadith about washing hands after sleep as a precaution against unseen impurity, implying that impurity is effective even without apparent change. (6) The hadith about the dog's lapping, which washes even though the dog's saliva does not change the water. Abu Hanifa concludes that wherever there is a strong presumption of impurity, the water is impermissible; no specific quantity is specified by revelation. The text also discusses an argument related to Malik and three times the amount, which seems to address a different point about water exiting a pure trough.

Key Terms
قلتين (qullatayn): Two qullahs, a measure of water volume. A qullah is estimated as about 100 liters (varies). Two qullahs thus equals approximately 200 liters.
بئر بضاعة (bi'r buda'ah): A well in Medina known for receiving runoff water that might contain impurities. Used in the debate to support the Hanafi view that running water does not become impure easily.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary hadith evidence used by Imam al-Shafi'i to argue that large quantities of water do not become impure from contact with impurity?
A) The hadith about washing hands after waking up
B) The hadith 'When water reaches two qullahs, it does not carry impurity'
C) The hadith about the dog's lapping
D) The hadith about not urinating in stagnant water

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that water becomes impure upon contact with any impurity, rejecting the Shafi'i threshold of two qullahs, based on a range of textual and analogical evidences.
