Book of Purity: Water becomes used (musta'mal) by removing ritual impurity (hadath). Thus it is like when a junub, menstruating woman, or person in minor impurity inserts his hand into water; it does not become used due to necessity. Analogically, it is used in their view for removing hadath, but it is dropped due to need. The commentator Kamal al-Din ibn al-Humam and al-Zayla'i confirmed this. Al-Bada'i' states that the dispute is not transmitted from them textually, but their cases indicate it. Similarly in al-Muhit, but he said: This dispute is correct according to Muhammad because the change of water according to Muhammad is due to performing an act of qurbah (drawing near to Allah), not because of the transfer of a legal impurity to the water. According to them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), the water changes because a legal impurity transfers to it. In both cases, a legal impurity transfers to the water, causing its change. What indicates the validity of the dispute is what is transmitted in al-Muhit, al-Khulasah, and many books, attributed by al-Hindi to the Salat al-Athar of Muhammad: If a man takes water in his mouth while junub and does not intend rinsing, then washes his hand with it, it suffices for washing his hand and does not become used according to Muhammad due to lack of intent of qurbah, even though hadath is removed from the mouth. But Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi says that Muhammad only did not deem it used due to necessity, not because removing hadath does not cause isti'mal. He explained in al-Muhit: 'He did not rule it used due to necessity.' This is supported by what is in Fath al-Qadir: 'What we understand is that both the qurbah that erases sins and the discharge (of obligation) affect change. Do you not see that the attribute of qurbah in voluntary charity had an effect of change until it was prohibited for the Prophet? Then we saw the effect when the attribute of discharge was established alongside it, which is stronger, so it was prohibited for his supporting relatives. Thus we know that each causes a legal change. By this, Muhammad's statement that it is only qurbah is weakened, unless it is said that this is not his madhhab.' If he washes his hand for food or from it, the water becomes used because he performs a qurbah, as it is sunnah. If he washes his hand from dirt, it does not become used due to lack of removing hadath or performing qurbah. This is in al-Muhit. This reasoning indicates that he was in a state of wudu, which is necessary. His statement 'because he performs a qurbah' indicates that he intended to perform the sunnah. If he did not intend it, it becomes used? There is a discussion. And in it: If a human hair reaches his mount and she washes that attached hair, the water does not become used. If he washes the head of a killed person that has separated from the body, the water becomes used because the head, when attached to the body, is considered part of the body and is prayed upon, so it is like the body. Hair is not considered part of the body, so when separated it has no ruling of the body, so its washing water is not used. Al-Walwaliji said in his Fatawa: This distinction applies on the preferred narration that human hair is not impure. On the other narration, it does not apply because it is impure and contaminates the water. In al-Muntagha and others: His statement: 'And discharge has an effect on change' is conjuncted to 'qurbah'. His statement: 'If he did not intend it, it does not become used' in al-Nahr: 'Accordingly, one should stipulate it in every sunnah like rinsing the mouth and nose and similar, and there is hesitation in that.' Al-Ramli said: I say there is no hesitation, as there is no impediment to stipulating it, even if he is not junub. And if he intends by washing the nose and mouth and teaching wudu to people, it does not become used if he does not intend prayer but rather teaching. It is not hidden that teaching is a qurbah. So if he intends to perform a qurbah, it should become used, like washing hands for food, for he does not intend prayer but rather performing a qurbah. This is supported by what is in Sharh al-Niqayah: 'A qurbah is what is attached to a legal ruling being deserving of reward. There is no doubt that teaching has a reward intended.' It may be answered that this water is not used for a qurbah because the qurbah is not in its use but in the teaching. Hence if he teaches verbally, he is independent of this act, unlike washing hands for food where the qurbah is only achieved by using it, so they differed. In al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah: The washing water of a deceased is impure, as Muhammad stated absolutely in al-Asl. The sound view is that if there is no impurity on his body, the water becomes used and is not impure. But Muhammad spoke absolutely because his washing water is rarely free from impurity. In al-Khulasah: If a boy performs wudu in a basin, does the water become used? The chosen view is that it becomes used if the boy is intelligent. We have already given the ruling if he inserts his hand into the vessel, so refer back. In al-Khulasah: If he takes water in his mouth not intending rinsing, it does not become used according to Muhammad. Similarly, if he takes it in his mouth and washes his limbs with it. Abu Yusuf said: It does not remain purifying, and this is correct. Know that this and similar examples, like their statement in the case of one who inserts his hands to the elbows or one of his feet into a basin, the water becomes used, indicate that water becomes used in three ways: Either by removing hadath with or without qurbah; or by performing a qurbah with or without removal of hadath; or by fulfilling an obligation. For in these cases, hadath and janabah are not removed from the washed limb, as it is known that hadath and janabah do not become... and similar mere cleaning and removal of dirt and filth, not performing a qurbah, does not make it used. Contemplate. Shaykh Isma'il said: Intention, like detailed, may be general; like intentional, may be implicit. So if one intends wudu in the manner of sunnah, similar enters into it implicitly. There is nothing in al-Bahr to specify each individually, so contemplate. His statement (the sound view that if there is no impurity on his body…) I say: Something similar will be mentioned from al-Siraj in the chapter on impurities, but it will come in Funerals that the impurity of the deceased is impurity of filth or ritual impurity, and that the author of al-Muhit argued for the first by saying that if it falls into a little water before washing, it contaminates it, and if one prays carrying the deceased, it is not permissible. The author of al-Muhit deemed that sound and attributed it in al-Bada'i' to the general body of scholars. This indicates that Muhammad's statement here is absolute that his washing water is impure, unless it is said that its contaminating little water and the invalidity of the prayer of its carrier are due to the impurity that is usually present, which is a far-fetched interpretation because the origin is purity, and one does not rule the water or prayer corrupt due to doubt, and similarly its washing water. Contemplate. His statement (As for when a boy performs wudu…) in al-Khaniyyah: An intelligent boy, if he performs wudu intending purification, should make the water used because he intended a considered qurbah. So his statement 'intending purification' indicates that if he does not intend purification, it does not become used. And in his statement 'should' there is an indication that there is no narration from…
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a detailed commentary on the ruling of water becoming musta'mal (used) and the different opinions within the Hanafi school on the effective cause ('illa) of that change. The passage type is an intra-Hanafi dispute, primarily between Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani and his teachers, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. The central question is: what causes water to become musta'mal (and thus no longer valid for purification)? Two views are presented: (1) The majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that the removal of hadath (ritual impurity) itself transfers a legal impurity (najasah hukmiyyah) to the water, making it musta'mal, regardless of intention. (2) Imam Muhammad holds that water becomes musta'mal only when used with the intent of drawing near to Allah (qurbah), such as in wudu or ghusl with the proper intention. The commentary then explores various applications and exceptions, such as the case of necessity (darurah) where the ruling is lifted, washing hands for food (a sunnah, so it involves qurbah), washing hands from dirt (no qurbah), washing a dead person's head vs. hair, and the case of a child performing wudu. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of the majority: water becomes musta'mal by the mere removal of hadath, whether or not one intends qurbah. However, the passage also notes that some scholars reconcile Muhammad's view by limiting it to cases of necessity. The commentary explains the legal reasoning and the practical consequences of each view.

Key Terms
مستعمل (musta'mal): Water that has been used for purification (wudu or ghusl) and is therefore considered tahir (pure) but not mutahhir (purifying) — it cannot be used again for wudu.
قربة (qurbah): An act of obedience intended to draw near to Allah, such as performing a commanded act like wudu or ghusl with proper intention. In this passage, it is the effective cause according to Imam Muhammad.
حدث (hadath): Ritual impurity, either minor (hadath asghar) or major (janabah, hayd, nifas). Removing hadath by wudu or ghusl is the act that, according to the majority, renders water musta'mal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school, what is the primary cause for water to become musta'mal (used)?
A) The intention of drawing near to Allah (qurbah).
B) The removal of ritual impurity (hadath), regardless of intention.
C) The physical change in the water's colour, taste, or smell.
D) The water being used specifically for washing the hands before food.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that water becomes musta'mal by the mere removal of hadath, without requiring intention of qurbah.

Water Used for Teaching Wudu – Does It Become Musta'mal?
Debating whether water becomes musta'mal when used for teaching wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on whether water used for teaching wudu becomes musta'mal and distinguish between direct and indirect qurbah.

Core Idea
Teaching wudu does not make water musta'mal because the qurbah is in the teaching, not the water use.

This passage from Bahru al-Raiq addresses a subtle question: if someone uses water to demonstrate wudu for teaching, does that water become musta'mal (used, no longer purifying)? The text compares this to washing hands before food, which is considered a qurbah and does make water musta'mal. We'll explore the reasoning behind the differing view and the key distinction between direct and indirect acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Positions
Determine which position is presented first (water becomes musta'mal) and which is the counter-argument (water does not become musta'mal).
The passage starts with a claim from Sharh al-Niqayah that teaching is a qurbah, so water should become musta'mal.
2
Understand the Analogy with Washing Hands for Food
Note how washing hands for food (ghusl al-yadayn li'l-ta'am) is used as an analogy: both are qurbah, but in one case water becomes musta'mal.
Washing hands for food is a recommended act (mustahabb) and is a qurbah; water used for it becomes musta'mal according to the view being challenged.
3
Analyze the Counter-Argument: Direct vs. Indirect Qurbah
The response argues that the qurbah in teaching lies in the teaching itself, not in the use of water. One could teach verbally, so the water use is incidental. In contrast, washing hands for food requires water use to fulfill the qurbah.
Key phrase: 'القربة فيه ليست استعماله إنما هي بسبب تعليمه' – the qurbah is not in its use but due to teaching.
4
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf (Practical Consequence)
If water for teaching does not become musta'mal, it remains tahur (pure and purifying) and can be used for wudu. If it becomes musta'mal, it is only tahir (pure) and cannot be used for wudu again.
The text concludes with 'فافترقا' (they differ), indicating the counter-argument is accepted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبتعليم الوضوء للناس لا يصير مستعملاً إذا لم يرد به الصلاة بل أراد تعليمه ا هـ . ولا يخفى أن التعليم قربة فإذا قصد إقامة القربة ينبغي أن يصير الماء مستعملاً كغسل اليدين للطعام فإنه لم يرد به الصلاة بل إقامة القربة كما لا يخفى، ويؤيده ما في شرح النقاية أوّلاً أن القربة ما تعلق به حكم شرعي وهو استحقاق الثواب، ولا شك أن في التعليم المقصود ثواباً. وقد يجاب عنه بأن هذا الماء لم يستعمل لقربة لأن القربة فيه ليست استعماله إنما هي بسبب تعليمه ولذا لو علمه بالقول استغني عن هذا الفعل بخلاف غسل اليدين من الطعام فإن القربة فيه لا تحصل إلا باستعماله فافترقا.
And by teaching wudu to people, it (water) does not become musta'mal if he did not intend prayer by it but rather intended teaching it. It is not hidden that teaching is a qurbah (act of drawing near to Allah). So if he intended performing the qurbah, it is appropriate that the water becomes musta'mal, like washing hands for food, for he did not intend prayer by it but rather performing the qurbah. This is supported by what is in Sharh al-Niqayah: first, that qurbah is that which is attached to a shar'i ruling, which is deserving of reward, and there is no doubt that in teaching intended there is reward. And it can be answered that this water was not used for a qurbah because the qurbah in it is not its use but rather due to his teaching; therefore if he taught by speech, this action would be unnecessary, unlike washing hands for food, for the qurbah in it is not obtained except by using it, so they differ.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether water becomes musta'mal when used for teaching wudu. The author presents a view that teaching is a qurbah, so water should become musta'mal, analogous to washing hands for food (which is a permissible act but not for prayer, yet washing hands for food is considered a qurbah by some). However, the counter-argument distinguishes: in teaching, the qurbah lies in the teaching itself, not in the use of water; one could teach verbally. In washing hands for food, the qurbah is in the actual use of water, so water becomes musta'mal. This is a nuanced discussion on the role of intention and directness of the qurbah.

Key Terms
مستعمل (musta'mal): Water that has been used for a qurbah or removal of hadath, thereby losing its purifying quality for wudu.
قربة (qurbah): An act of drawing near to Allah, i.e., an act of worship or obedience that brings reward.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because teaching is not a qurbah.
B) Because the qurbah in teaching lies in the teaching itself, not in the water use, unlike washing hands for food where the qurbah is in using water.
C) Because washing hands for food is obligatory, while teaching is optional.
D) Because the teacher intends prayer, not teaching.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, water used for teaching wudu does not become musta'mal because the qurbah lies in the instruction, not the water itself, distinguishing it from acts where water use is essential to the qurbah.

Ruling on Water Used for Washing the Deceased
Intra-Hanafi dispute on water from ghusl mayyit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on water used for washing the deceased and distinguish between the absolute view of Imam Muhammad and the preferred view (al-asahh).

Core Idea
Water from ghusl mayyit is musta'mal if the body is pure; otherwise, it is najis.

This lesson examines a passage from al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah that addresses the status of water used to wash a deceased person. Imam Muhammad initially ruled that such water is absolutely impure (najis). However, later Hanafi scholars refined this: if the deceased's body is free from external impurities, the water becomes musta'mal (used water) — pure in itself but not purifying. This distinction is essential for correctly applying the rules of taharah in funeral rites.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the water that results from washing a deceased body. Two rulings are presented: absolute najis (Muhammad) and conditionally musta'mal (al-asahh).
2
Locate the dalil
The passage cites Imam Muhammad's statement in al-Asl and then the preferred view from al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah. The evidence for the preferred view is the absence of external najis.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The preferred view relies on the principle that water is considered pure unless proven impure. The body's state determines the water's status.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is a disagreement within the Hanafi school: Muhammad's unconditional statement versus the conditioned preferred view.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The later scholars (as reflected in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah) adopt the preferred view (al-asahh) because Muhammad's ruling is explained by the common presence of impurity on bodies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الفتاوى الظهيرية : وغسالة الميت نجسة كذا أطلق محمد في الأصل والأصح أنه إذا لم يكن على بدنه نجاسة يصير الماء مستعملاً ولا يكون نجساً إلا أن محمداً إنما أطلق الماء لأن غسالته لا تخلو عن النجاسة غالباً.
And in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah: The washing water of the deceased is najis (impure) - thus Imam Muhammad said absolutely in al-Asl. But the most correct view is that if there is no impurity on his body, the water becomes musta'mal and is not najis, except that Muhammad's absolute statement is because his washing water is rarely free from impurity.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling regarding the water used to wash the deceased (ghusl mayyit). Imam Muhammad ruled in al-Asl (one of the zahir al-riwayah books) that this water is absolutely najis. However, the sahih (correct) view according to later scholars is that if the deceased's body is free from physical impurities (najis), the water becomes musta'mal (used water) and not najis. Muhammad's unconditional statement is explained by the fact that a deceased body is rarely free from impurities, so his ruling covers the common case. This is important because musta'mal water is still tahir (pure) though not tahur (purifying for wudu), whereas najis water is impure and cannot be used. The preferred view (al-asahh) thus distinguishes based on the actual condition of the body.

Key Terms
غسالة ميت (ghussalat al-mayyit): The water that drips off the deceased during ghusl (ritual washing).
مستعمل (musta'mal): Water that has been used in an obligatory purification and is no longer tahur (purifying), but remains tahir (pure).
الأصح (al-asahh): The most correct view according to later Hanafi scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is najis (impure).
B) It is musta'mal (used water).
C) It is tahur (purifying).
D) It is makruh.

Key Takeaway
The most correct Hanafi view distinguishes based on the presence of external impurity on the deceased's body.

Wudu of a Child and Water Taken into the Mouth
Rulings on musta'mal water from child's wudu and mouth rinsing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on when water becomes musta'mal in the cases of a child's wudu and unintentional mouth rinsing, and identify the preferred view (Abu Yusuf) regarding mouth water.

Core Idea
Intention determines musta'mal for child's wudu; for mouth water, act suffices per Abu Yusuf.

This lesson examines two specific cases from al-Khulasa that clarify the boundary of musta'mal water. The first case involves a rational child performing wudu – does the water become used? The second addresses a person who takes water into his mouth without intending the sunnah of madmadah. An intra-Hanafi disagreement between Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf is resolved, with Abu Yusuf's view declared sahih. Understanding these rulings helps you apply the concept of qurbah (drawing near to Allah) to the status of water.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two legal issues
The passage presents two distinct scenarios: (1) a child performing wudu in a basin, and (2) a person taking water into the mouth without the intention of madmadah.
2
Determine the ruling for the child's wudu
The text states al-mukhtar (the preferred view) that water becomes musta'mal if the child is rational (sabi aqil). The child's act is a valid qurbah, so it affects the water's purity.
A 'rational child' (mumayyiz) is typically around 7 years old.
3
Analyze the disagreement on mouth water
Imam Muhammad holds that water taken into the mouth without intent does not become musta'mal. Abu Yusuf holds that it does not remain tahur (purifying). Note the basis: Muhammad requires intention of qurbah, Abu Yusuf considers even unintentional entry as rendering water musta'mal.
The disagreement is between two senior Hanafi imams.
4
Identify the tarjih (preference)
The author of al-Khulasa declares Abu Yusuf's view as 'al-sahih' (the correct view). Thus the mufta bihi is that water taken into the mouth becomes musta'mal regardless of intention.
Tarjih authority: al-Khulasa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الخلاصة: أما إذا توضأ الصبي في طست هل يصير الماء مستعملاً؟ والمختار أنه يصير مستعملاً إذا كان الصبي عاقلاً ا.هـ. ... وفي الخلاصة: ولو أخذ الماء بفمه لا يريد به المضمضة لا يصير مستعملاً عند محمد، وكذا لو أخذ بفيه وغسل أعضاءه بذلك. وقال أبو يوسف : لا يبقى طهوراً وهو الصحيح ا هـ .
And in al-Khulasa: As for when a child performs wudu in a basin, does the water become musta'mal? The chosen view is that it becomes musta'mal if the child is intelligent (rational). ... And in al-Khulasa: If one takes water into his mouth not intending madmadah, it does not become musta'mal according to Muhammad, and likewise if he takes it into his mouth and washes his limbs with that. Abu Yusuf said: It does not remain tahur (purifying), and that is the correct view.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage contains two related rulings. First: If a rational child (sabi aqil) performs wudu in a vessel, the water becomes musta'mal according to the preferred view (al-mukhtar), because the child's act is a valid qurbah. Second: If an adult takes water into his mouth without intending madmadah (rinsing, which is a sunnah), then according to Imam Muhammad, the water does not become musta'mal because there was no intention of qurbah. But Abu Yusuf says it does not remain tahur (i.e., becomes musta'mal), and this is considered the sahih (correct) view. This demonstrates a disagreement between Muhammad and Abu Yusuf on whether the mere act of taking water into the mouth (without intent) renders it musta'mal. The preferred view is that of Abu Yusuf.

Key Terms
صبي عاقل (sabi aqil): A child who has reached the age of discernment (mumayyiz), typically around 7 years old.
مضمضة (madmadah): Rinsing the mouth as a sunnah of wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It becomes musta'mal (used water).
B) It remains tahur (purifying).
C) It becomes najis (impure).
D) It is makruh but still purifying.

Key Takeaway
Water becomes musta'mal both when a rational child performs wudu (mukhtar) and when water enters the mouth even without intention (mufta bihi per Abu Yusuf).

Isqat al-Fard: The Third Cause of Musta'mal Water
Explaining the three causes of musta'mal water and rejecting the divisibility of hadath.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three causes of musta'mal water and explain the distinction between isqat al-fard and removal of hadath.

Core Idea
Fulfilling an obligation (isqat al-fard) makes water musta'mal even if hadath is not removed — they are distinct.

This lesson refines the Hanafi understanding of musta'mal water. While many know that removing hadath or performing a qurbah makes water musta'mal, a third, less-known cause is isqat al-fard. We will explore why this distinction matters and how it resolves apparent contradictions in the rulings of wudu.

Guided Path
1
State the known causes
Recall the two standard causes: removal of hadath (hadath) and performing a qurbah (worship act).
These are well-established in the madhhab.
2
Identify the third cause: isqat al-fard
Recognize that when an obligation (fard) for a specific limb is fulfilled, the water used becomes musta'mal, even if hadath remains.
This is based on a transmission from Hasan ibn Ziyad from Abu Hanifa.
3
Understand the non-relationship
Isqat al-fard does not automatically imply hadath removal; they can occur separately.
Hadath is an indivisible state; partial removal is impossible.
4
Apply to a concrete example
Consider a person with hadath who inserts only their hand into a vessel without necessity: the water becomes musta'mal because the fard of washing that hand is fulfilled, even though hadath persists until the remaining limbs are washed.
This clarifies the practical implication.
5
Recognize the source authority
Note that this view is from the Nawadir (rare transmissions), not Zahir al-Riwayah. Al-Marghinani in Fath al-Qadir supports it.
The mufta bihi position accepts this cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يتجزآن زوالاً كما لا يتجزآن ثبوتاً قالوا وهذا هو الصحيح وكذا لم توجد نية القربة وإنما سقط الفرض عن العضو المغسول فكان الأولى ذكر هذا السبب الثالث، ولا تلازم بين سقوط الفرض وارتفاع الحدث، فسقوط الفرض عن اليد مثلاً يقتضي أن لا يجب إعادة غسلها مع بقية الأعضاء ويكون ارتفاع الحدث موقوفاً على غسل الباقي، وسقوط الفرض هو الأصل في الاستعمال إلا أن يقال: إن الحدث زال عن العضو زوالاً موقوفاً لكن المعلل به في الحسن عن أبي حنيفة كما نقله في فتح القدير إسقاط الفرض في مسألة إدخال اليد الإناء لغير ضرورة لا إزالة الحدث.
They are not divisible in removal just as they are not divisible in establishment. They said: This is correct. And likewise the intention of qurbah was not found, but the obligation (fard) fell from the washed limb, so it was better to mention this third cause. And there is no necessary connection between the falling of the obligation (isqat al-fard) and the removal of hadath. So the falling of the obligation from the hand, for example, entails that its washing need not be repeated along with the remaining limbs, and the removal of hadath is contingent upon washing the rest. And isqat al-fard is the basis for isti'mal (water becoming musta'mal), except that it may be said: The hadath left the limb in a conditional removal, but the cause (al-mu'allal bihi) in al-Hasan's transmission from Abu Hanifa, as quoted in Fath al-Qadir, is isqat al-fard in the case of inserting the hand into the vessel without necessity, not removal of hadath.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq refines the understanding of what makes water musta'mal. The discussion centers on whether there are two or three causes. The standard two are: (1) removal of hadath, (2) performing a qurbah. A third cause is suggested: isqat al-fard (fulfilling an obligation), as when someone washes a limb in wudu, the obligation for that limb falls, even if hadath is not fully removed (because other limbs remain). The text clarifies that isqat al-fard does not necessarily imply removal of hadath; they are separate. The example given is washing one hand in a small vessel without necessity: according to Abu Hanifa, this makes the water musta'mal because the obligation for that hand is fulfilled, even if the person's hadath is not fully removed until complete wudu. This is based on a riwayah from Hasan ibn Ziyad. Thus, the cause is isqat al-fard, not removal of hadath. The passage also states that hadath (and janabah) cannot be partially removed—they either exist or not, but the fard obligation can fall partially.

Key Terms
إسقاط الفرض (isqat al-fard): The falling of the obligation (to wash a specific limb) from the person, making the water used for that wash musta'mal.
حدث (hadath): Ritual impurity that requires wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in this passage, what is the basis for water becoming musta'mal when someone washes a limb without completing wudu (e.g., inserting hand into water)?
A) Removal of hadath from that limb.
B) Intention of qurbah.
C) Isqat al-fard (fulfillment of obligation) for that limb.
D) The water becomes najis.

Key Takeaway
Isqat al-fard is a distinct cause for musta'mal water, separate from hadath removal, and hadath itself cannot be partially eliminated.

The Two Meanings of Hadath and Suqut al-Fard
Definition of hadath and its divisibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi meanings of hadath and explain why suqut al-fard does not necessarily imply irtifa' al-hadath.

Core Idea
Hadath as prevention is indivisible; as virtual impurity it is divisible – and suqut al-fard is not the same as removal.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author delves into a subtle distinction that many students overlook: the difference between hadath as a legal prevention and hadath as a virtual impurity. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying rulings related to water becoming musta'mal and the relationship between dropping an obligation and the actual removal of impurity. We will also see that the dropping of the obligation to wash a limb does not automatically mean the hadath has been removed from that limb.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two meanings of hadath
Locate in the text where Shaykh Qasim distinguishes between hadath as legal prevention (man'iyya) and as virtual impurity (najasa hukmiyya). Note that the first is indivisible, the second is divisible.
The two meanings are based on different conceptualizations of what hadath is.
2
Understand the indivisibility of the first meaning
Hadath as man'iyya does not come off limb by limb; it is fully removed only when purification is complete. This is agreed upon by Abu Hanifa and his companions.
This means you cannot be 'half pure' in the sense of prevention.
3
Understand the divisibility of the second meaning
Hadath as najasa hukmiyya can be removed from individual limbs, and water becomes musta'mal by removing this type from a limb. This is also agreed upon.
This divisibility is what explains cases like the well issue where suqut al-fard occurs.
4
Analyze the relationship between suqut al-fard and irtifa' al-hadath
The text denies a necessary correlation: suqut al-fard can occur without irtifa' al-hadath (e.g., incomplete wudu) and irtifa' al-hadath can occur without suqut al-fard (e.g., wudu of a discerning child).
The key is that suqut al-fard is about obligation, while irtifa' al-hadath is about actual purity.
5
Evaluate the reward for partial washing
The passage concludes that reward for washing individual limbs is conditional on completing the wudu, supported by the hadith about sins leaving with the last drop.
This reinforces that the complete act is what matters for reward, not the partial removal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة يتجزآن زوالاً كما لا يتجزآن ثبوتاً قالوا وهذا هو الصحيح وكذا لم توجد نية القربة وإنما سقط الفرض عن العضو المغسول فكان الأولى ذكر هذا السبب الثالث، ولا تلازم بين سقوط الفرض وارتفاع الحدث، فسقوط الفرض عن اليد مثلاً يقتضي أن لا يجب إعادة غسلها مع بقية الأعضاء ويكون ارتفاع الحدث موقوفاً على غسل الباقي، وسقوط الفرض هو الأصل في الاستعمال إلا أن يقال: إن الحدث زال عن العضو زوالاً موقوفاً لكن المعلل به في الحسن عن أبي حنيفة كما نقله في فتح القدير إسقاط الفرض في مسألة إدخال اليد الإناء لغير ضرورة لا إزالة الحدث. وفي الخلاصة : لو غسل المحدث عضواً آخر سوی أعضاء الوضوء كتاب الحدث صاحب المذهب كما قال في القنية قوله : (لما عرف أن الحدث والجنابة (الخ) قال الشيخ قاسم في حواشي المجمع الحدث يقال بمعنيين بمعنى المانعية الشرعية عما لا يحل بدون الطهارة وهذا لا يتجزئ بلا خلاف عند أبي حنيفة وصاحبيه وبمعنى النجاسة الحكمية وهذا يتجزأ ثبوتاً وارتفاعاً بلا خلاف عند أبي حنيفة وأصحابه وصيرورة الماء مستعملاً بإزالة الثانية ففي مسألة البئر سقط الفرض عن الرجلين بلا خلاف والماء الذي أسقط الفرض صار مستعملاً بلا خلاف على الصحيح اهـ. هذا هو التحقيق فخذه فإنه بالأخذ حقيق. كذا في حاشية نوح أفندي على الدرر . قوله : (ولا تلازم الخ) المراد نفي التلازم من أحد الجانبين وهو جانب سقوط الفرض أي فإنه قد يسقط الفرض ويرتفع الحدث كما إذا أتم الطهارة وقد يسقط ولا يرتفع الحدث كما إذا لم يتمها، وأما جانب رفع ا فإنه إذا وجد لزم منه سقوط الفرض، وقد يقال : لا تلازم من هذا الجانب أيضاً فإنه قد يرتفع الحدث ولا يسقط الفرض كوضوء الصبي العاقل لما مر من صيرورة مائه مستعملاً . مع أنه لا فرض عليه. بقي هل بين سقوط الفرض والقربة تلازم أم لا ؟ إن قلنا إن إسقاط الفرض لا ثواب فيه فلا، وإن قلنا فيه ثواب فنعم. قال العلامة المحقق نوح أفندي : والذي يقتضيه النظر الصحيح أن الراجح الأول لأن الثواب في الوضوء المقصود وهو شرعاً عبارة عن غسل الأعضاء الثلاثة ومسح الرأس فغسل عضو منها ليس بوضوء شرعي فكيف يثاب عليه اللهم إلا أن يقال : إنه يثاب على غسل كل عضو منها ثواباً موقوفاً على الإتمام فإن أتمه أثيب على غسل كل عضو منها وإلا فلا، ويدل عليه ما أخرجه مسلم عن أبي هريرة رضي الله تعالى عنه قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «إذا توضأ العبد المسلم أو المؤمن فغسل وجهه خرج من وجهه كل خطيئة نظر إليها بعينه مع الماء أو مع آخر قطر الماء، فإذا غسل يده خرج من يده كل خطيئة بطشتها يده مع الماء أو مع آخر قطر الماء، فإذا غسل رجليه خرج كل خطيئة مشتها رجلاه مع الماء أو مع آخر قطر الماء حتى يخرج نقياً من الذنوب والآثام (۱) اهـ
The Book of Purification. They are not divisible in removal just as they are not divisible in establishment. They said: this is the correct view. Similarly, the intention of drawing near (qurbah) was not found, rather the obligation (fard) dropped from the washed limb. So it was better to mention this third cause. There is no necessary correlation between the dropping of the obligation and the removal of the event (hadath). For example, dropping the obligation from the hand requires that it is not obligatory to rewash it along with the remaining limbs, and the removal of the event is conditional upon washing the rest. The dropping of the obligation is the basis in usage, except if it is said that the event was removed from the limb with a suspended removal, but the reasoning in al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa, as transmitted in Fath al-Qadir, is the dropping of the obligation in the issue of inserting the hand into the vessel without necessity, not the removal of the event. In al-Khulasa: If a person in minor impurity washes another limb besides the limbs of wudu... The book of hadath, the author of the madhhab as said in al-Quniya. His statement: (Since it is known that hadath and janabah...) Shaykh Qasim said in the margins of al-Majma': hadath is used in two meanings: (1) the meaning of legal prevention from what is not permissible without purification, and this is indivisible without disagreement according to Abu Hanifa and his two companions; (2) the meaning of virtual impurity (najasa hukmiyya), and this is divisible in establishment and removal without disagreement according to Abu Hanifa and his companions. And water becoming used (musta'mal) is by removal of the second. In the well issue, the obligation dropped from the two feet without disagreement, and the water that dropped the obligation became musta'mal without disagreement on the correct view. This is the verification, so take it, for it is worthy of being taken. Similarly in the gloss of Nuh Afandi on al-Durar. His statement: (And there is no correlation...). The intended meaning is negation of correlation from one side, which is the side of dropping the obligation: i.e., the obligation may drop and the event may be removed, as when he completes purification; and it may drop without removal, as when he does not complete it. As for the side of removal, when it occurs, it necessarily entails dropping the obligation. But it may be said that there is no correlation from this side either, because the event may be removed without the obligation dropping, like the wudu of a discerning child, due to what has passed about his water becoming musta'mal, even though there is no obligation on him. Remaining: Is there correlation between dropping the obligation and qurbah or not? If we say that dropping the obligation has no reward, then no; if we say there is reward, then yes. The investigating scholar Nuh Afandi said: What sound consideration requires is that the first is preponderant, because reward is in the intended wudu, which legally is washing the three limbs and wiping the head. Washing one of them is not legally wudu, so how can one be rewarded for it? Unless it is said that one is rewarded for washing each limb with a reward suspended upon completion: if he completes it, he is rewarded for washing each limb; otherwise not. This is supported by what Muslim narrated from Abu Hurayra radiya Allahu 'anhu: the Messenger of Allah (s) said: 'When the Muslim or believing servant performs wudu, and washes his face, every sin that his eyes looked at comes out from his face with the water or with the last drop of water... until he emerges free of sins and misdeeds.'
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq defines the concept of hadath and its relationship to suqut al-fard (dropping of obligation) and irtifa' al-hadath (removal of impurity). The author explains that hadath in the sense of legal prevention (man'iyya) is indivisible: once purification is complete, the entire hadath is removed; it does not come off limb by limb. However, hadath in the sense of virtual impurity (najasa hukmiyya) is divisible. The key point is that the dropping of the obligation to wash a limb (e.g., when reusing water from a well) does not necessarily mean the hadath has been removed from that limb. The author rejects a necessary correlation between suqut al-fard and irtifa' al-hadath, citing the case of a child's wudu where hadath is removed but no obligation exists. He then discusses whether suqut al-fard carries reward and concludes that reward is only for the complete wudu, as supported by the hadith of Abu Hurayra.

Key Terms
حدث (hadath): Legal prevention from acts requiring purity, or virtual impurity (najasa hukmiyya).
سقوط الفرض (suqut al-fard): The dropping of the obligation to wash a particular limb, e.g., when water becomes musta'mal after washing it.
ماء مستعمل (mā' musta'mal): Water that has been used for a valid ablution or cleansing, rendering it ritually used and not suitable for further purification.
ارتفاع الحدث (irtifa' al-hadath): The removal of the virtual impurity (najasa hukmiyya) from a limb; in the context of this passage, it is distinct from suqut al-fard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, water becomes musta'mal when it:
A) Contacts the limb during wudu
B) Separates from the limb after causing the obligation to drop (suqut al-fard)
C) Becomes dirty with visible impurities
D) Is used to wash a limb that still has hadath

Key Takeaway
Hadath has two Hanafi meanings: one indivisible (prevention) and one divisible (virtual impurity); suqut al-fard is the criterion for water becoming musta'mal, not the removal of hadath.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
12 min
When Water Becomes Musta'mal: Separation vs. Contact
Determining the moment water becomes musta'mal and related rulings on moisture transfer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when water becomes musta'mal and explain the evidence from prohibition of transferring moisture.

Core Idea
Water becomes musta'mal only after separating from the limb, not upon contact, to avoid hardship.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq settles a key point in Hanafi fiqh: does water become used (musta'mal) the moment it touches the limb during wudu, or only after it leaves the limb? The Hanafi school chooses the latter, supported by the rule against transferring moisture from a washed limb to another. We will trace the reasoning, the opposing view of Sufyan al-Thawri, and the special cases that reinforce the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
State clearly the Hanafi position: water becomes musta'mal when it separates from the limb, not upon contact, and it does not need to settle in a place.
This is the mufta bihi position from the Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Understand the opposing view
Sufyan al-Thawri held that water becomes musta'mal only after it leaves the body and settles in a container or on the ground. Note the practical difference: for example, using leftover moisture on a limb is valid for washing another part according to him, but invalid according to Hanafis.
The text mentions his reliance on cases like taking moisture from a washed limb to wash another part.
3
Analyze the Hanafi evidence
The key evidence is that transferring moisture from a washed limb (e.g., beard) to a wiped part (head) is invalid, indicating the water is still 'in use' while on the limb. Also, the principle of hardship (haraj) prevents strict analogy on contact, which would require separate water for every part of the limb.
See the text: 'if he wipes his head with moisture from his beard, it is not valid'.
4
Apply to special cases
Work through the special rulings: washing a non-wudu limb does not make water musta'mal; the wudu of a menstruating woman does make it musta'mal because it is a valid recommended act; washing more than three times depends on intention (whether it is a new wudu or an addition).
These cases confirm the separation condition: the water is only considered 'used' after it leaves the limb in a valid purification act.
5
Link to the underlying usul
The ruling ties to a deeper question: does minor impurity (hadath) reside only on the limbs or the whole body? The preponderant Hanafi view is that it resides on the limbs, so water does not become musta'mal until it leaves them. This explains why water retains its purity while still on the limb.
This connection is mentioned toward the end of the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وفي الخلاصة لو غسل المحدث عضواً سوى أعضاء الوضوء) الأصح أنه لا مستعملاً. يصيره فإن قلت: على مقابل الأصح كيف يصير مستعملاً ولم يوجد واحد من الثلاثة؟ قلت قال في النهر : (۱) رواه مسلم في كتاب الطهارة حديث .۳۲ الموطأ في كتاب الطهارة حديث ٣١. أحمد في مسنده (۲/ (٢٦٣/٥) (۳۰۳ كالفخذ، الأصح إنه لا يصير مستعملاً بخلاف أعضاء الوضوء ا هـ. وفي المبتغي بالغين بالمعجمة وبغسله ثوباً أو دابة تؤكل لا . يصير مستعملاً، ووضوء الحائض مستعمل لأن وضوءها مستحب ا هـ . ولا يخفى أنه لا يصير مستعملاً إلا إذا قصدت الاتيان بالمستحب وفي البدائع : لو زاد على الثلاث فإن أراد بالزيادة ابتداء الوضوء صار الماء مستعملاً، وإن أراد الزيادة على الوضوء الأول اختلف المشايخ فيه ا هـ . وفيه كلام قدمناه في بحث تثليث الغسل في السنن فليراجع فإنه يقتضي أن الوضوء على الوضوء لا يكون قربة إلا إذا اختلف المجلس فحينئذ يكون قلنا : لما نوى القربة فقد ازداد طهارة على طهارة ولن تكون طهارة جديدة إلا بإزالة النجاسة الحكمية حكماً فصارت الطهارة على الطهارة وعلى الحدث سواء ا هـ . وأما الثاني أعني وقت ثبوت الاستعمال فقال بعض مشايخنا : الماء المستعمل ما زايل البدن واستقر في مكان من أرض أو إناء وهو مذهب سفيان الثوري، واستدل بمسائل زعم أنها تدل له منها إذا توضأ واغتسل وبقي على يده لمعة فأخذ البلل منها في الوضوء أو من أي عضو كان في الغسل وغسل اللمعة يجوز، ومنها نقل البلة من مغسول إلى ممسوح جائز وإن وجد الانفصال، ومنها أن الخرقة التي يتمسح بها تجوز الصلاة معها وإن كان ما أصابها من البلل كثيراً فاحشاً، وكذا إذا أصاب ثوبه الماء المستعمل لا يضره وإن كان كثيراً وإن وجد الانفصال فأما عندنا فما دام على العضو لا وإذا زايله صار مستعملاً وإن لم يستقر في مكان فإنه ذكر في الأصل أنه إذا مسح رأسه ببلل من لحيته لم يجز، وإن لم يستقر في مكان وكذا لو مسح رأسه ببلل باق بعد مسح الخفين لا يجزئه وعلل بأنه ماء قد مسح به مرة أشار به إلى ما قلنا. قالوا لا يجوز نقل البلة من عضو مغسول إلى مثله، فدل على أن المذهب ما قلناه ووجهه أن القياس صيرورته مستعملاً بنفس الملاقاة لوجود السبب فكان ينبغي أن يؤخذ لكل جزء من العضو جزء من الماء إلا أن فيه حرجاً فسقط اعتبار حالة الاستعمال في عضو واحد حقيقة أو في عضو واحد أخذه مستعملاً يصير الظاهر أن هذا له التفات إلى خلاف آخر هو أن الحدث الأصغر إذا وجد هل حلّ بكل البدن وجعل غسل أعضاء الوضوء رافعاً عن كل تخفيفاً أو بأعضاء الوضوء فقط قولان، وكان الراجح هو الثاني ولذا لم يصر الماء مستعملاً بخلافه على الأول قوله : (ووضوء الحائض مستعمل لأن وضوءها مستحب) قال في النهر : قالوا بوضوء الحائض يصير مستعملاً لأنه يستحب لها الوضوء لكل فريضة وأن تجلس في مصلاها قدرها كيلا تنسى عادتها ومقتضى كلامهم اختصاص ذلك بالفريضة وينبغي
His saying: (And in al-Khulasa: If a person in minor impurity washes a limb other than the limbs of wudu, like the thigh, the correct view is that it does not become musta'mal, contrary to the limbs of wudu). It (the footnote) says: Muslim narrated in the Book of Purification... In al-Muntabi (with ghayn and mujama): And washing a garment or an animal that is eaten does not make it musta'mal. The wudu of a menstruating woman is musta'mal because her wudu is recommended. It is not hidden that it does not become musta'mal unless she intends to perform the recommended act. In al-Bada'i: If he washes more than three times, if he intends by the extra wash to start a new wudu, the water becomes musta'mal; if he intends it as an addition to the first wudu, the scholars differed. There is a discussion we have presented in the discussion of washing three times among the sunan, so refer to it. It requires that wudu upon wudu is not a qurbah unless the sitting is different; then the water becomes musta'mal. If the sitting is the same, it is not a qurbah but disliked, so the water is not musta'mal. In Mi'raj al-Diraya: If it is said, 'The person performing wudu has no impurity, either real or virtual, on his limbs, so how does the water become musta'mal with the intention of qurbah?' We say: When he intends qurbah, he increases purity upon purity, and there would be no new purity except by removing virtual impurity juridically. So purity upon purity and upon hadath are the same. As for the second, i.e., the time of establishing usage, some of our scholars said: Used water is what leaves the body and settles in a place on the ground or a vessel. This is the madhhab of Sufyan al-Thawri. He argued with cases that he claimed support him, such as: if one performs wudu and ghusl and some moisture remains on his hand, then takes moisture from it for wudu or from any limb in ghusl and washes the remaining spot, it is permissible. Also, transferring moisture from a washed part to a wiped part is permissible even if there is separation. Also, the cloth with which one dries oneself, prayer is permissible with it even if the moisture on it is excessive. Similarly, if the musta'mal water gets on his garment, it does not harm, even if much and even if there is separation. But according to us: as long as it is on the limb, it is not musta'mal; when it leaves the limb, it becomes musta'mal, even if it does not settle in a place. For it is mentioned in al-Asl that if he wipes his head with moisture from his beard, it is not valid, even if it does not settle in a place. Similarly, if he wipes his head with remaining moisture after wiping the khuffs, it does not suffice him. It was explained that it is water that has been wiped with once, indicating what we said. They said: It is not permissible to transfer moisture from a washed limb to a similar one. This indicates that the madhhab is what we said. Its basis is that analogically (qiyas) water becomes musta'mal by mere contact due to the existence of the cause, so it would be necessary that for every part of the limb a part of water be taken, but there is hardship in that. So the consideration of the state of usage was dropped on a single limb, in reality or on a single limb... It appears that this takes into account another difference: whether minor impurity, when it exists, is distributed over the whole body and the washing of wudu limbs is made a remover for the whole as a concession, or only over the wudu limbs. There are two views. The preponderant is the second, and therefore water did not become musta'mal, contrary to the first view. His saying: (And the wudu of a menstruating woman is musta'mal because her wudu is recommended). He said in al-Nahr: They said that the wudu of a menstruating woman becomes musta'mal because it is recommended for her to perform wudu for every obligatory prayer and that she sit in her prayer place for its duration so as not to forget her habit. The implication of their speech is that it is specific to obligatory prayer, and it is appropriate...
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the conditions under which water becomes musta'mal (used) after being used for purification. The correct Hanafi position is that water becomes musta'mal only after it separates from the limb, not upon mere contact. This is contrasted with the view of Sufyan al-Thawri who held that water becomes musta'mal once it leaves the body and settles in a container or on the ground. The Hanafi position is supported by the rule that one cannot transfer moisture from a washed limb to another part (e.g., wiping the head with moisture from the beard is invalid). The passage also covers special cases: washing a non-wudu limb does not make water musta'mal, a menstruating woman's wudu makes water musta'mal because it is recommended, and washing more than three times depends on intention. The underlying principle is that water becomes musta'mal by separating from the limb, and this is linked to the nature of hadath: if minor impurity is considered to reside only on the limbs, water does not become musta'mal until it leaves them.

Key Terms
ماء مستعمل (mā' musta'mal): Water that has been used for a valid purification, rendering it ritually used and not pure enough for further purification.
نقل البلة (naql al-ballati): Transferring moisture from one washed part to another limb or part of the body during purification.
وضوء الحائض (wudū' al-hā'id): The wudu performed by a menstruating woman, which is recommended (mustahabb) not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is transferring moisture from a washed limb (e.g., beard) to another limb (e.g., head for wiping) invalid?
A) Because the water has already become najis.
B) Because the water is considered musta'mal while still on the washed limb.
C) Because the water is still considered 'in use' for the original limb and cannot be transferred.
D) Because transferring moisture is always allowed, but this specific case is an exception.

Key Takeaway
Water becomes musta'mal only after separating from the limb during purification, a ruling based on textual evidence and the principle of hardship.
